Merely Involved Procedures, Not Technical Issues

Naval Talks Aground: England, America and Japan Issue Simultaneous Statements; Suspension Until October 63

(London) The Foreign Office today issued a public statement declaring that the naval discussions between England, America and Japan are now exclusively concerned with procedural matters. Any further talks with Japan regarding other naval issues must be held around October, at which time the Japanese government will dispatch technical experts. Simultaneously, according to a Reuters dispatch from Tokyo, the postponement of the London naval talks until October has stirred repercussions. A high-level naval conference convened today and passed a resolution insisting that the ship replacement procedures recently agreed upon should be implemented immediately. Furthermore, according to a Reuters dispatch from Washington, Secretary of State Hull declared that the suspension of the initial London naval talks does not signify a rupture. Davis is prepared to go to London again when the Japanese government plans to send representatives. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull declared today that the preliminary naval conference will reconvene in London this autumn, pending the readiness of Japanese representatives to participate in negotiations. This is the primary reason for the temporary adjournment. At this time, American policy will also be re-discussed with the government by its representative, Davis, who has been ordered to return to the United States from London within the week. In a meeting with reporters, Secretary of State Hull stated that Davis's participation in the talks in London, as well as future consultations with England and Japan, should not be regarded as a formal conference, but merely an exchange of views to serve as the basis for formal preparatory meetings. Only after the formal preparatory meetings have been held can a decision be made as to whether it is necessary to hold a naval disarmament conference next year. Hull did not express his opinion on whether it is possible to hold such a conference under the current international situation. (National Telegraph, 16th)

(Tokyo) The naval conference preparatory talks held in London, after consultation between England, America, and Japan, decided to postpone the meeting until the end of October, etc. Details have been noted in previous telegrams. The British statement was issued in London today, and the Japanese Foreign Ministry simultaneously issued a statement with the same content at 11:30 a.m. Japan time, as follows:

Regarding the procedural issues of next year's naval conference, Ambassador Matsudaira to England, British Foreign Secretary Simon, and American representative Davis have conferred. As for other matters discussed with the Japanese representatives, the Japanese government will dispatch specialists separately, and will not hold talks before the end of October. (Dentsu dispatch, 17th)

Hiroshi Saito Arrives in Tokyo, Reports on Diplomatic Work with the United States, Offers Advice on Disarmament Issues to the Government, Will Inspect the Puppet State Before Returning to His Post in America by October 64

(Tokyo) Ambassador to the United States Saito visited Foreign Minister Hirota and Vice Minister Shigemitsu at the Foreign Ministry at 4:30 p.m. today, and described the circumstances of his safe return. He also reported in detail on the American sentiment towards Japan, with the Manchurian problem as its core, as well as the American public opinion on next year's disarmament conference, the policies of President Roosevelt and Secretary of State Hull, and various issues between Japan and the United States. He has made significant suggestions regarding Japanese-American diplomatic work. (Japan United Press dispatch, 17th)

(Tokyo) Ambassador Saito, who returned to the country today, immediately went to Tokyo to visit Foreign Minister Hirota. Although the United States now acknowledges Japan's actions after the Manchurian Incident as unavoidable, it is unwilling to abandon its traditional Far Eastern policy and opposes Japan's demand to break the ratio system. It was clearly stated in the Hirota-Hull exchange of documents that Japan could propose adjustments in the relations between the two countries. Therefore, Foreign Minister Hirota's adoption of such measures, regardless of the outcome of next year's naval conference, is not without significance. Depending on the method, it may lead to the success of next year's conference. If the United States is open-minded and accepts Japan's proposal, Japan may put forward a new proposal. Therefore, Ambassador Saito's advice is extremely noteworthy. (Dentsu dispatch, 17th)

Yokohama Ambassador to the United States Saito, accompanied by his wife, daughter, and others, arrived here on the Chichibu Maru on the 17th afternoon. According to his remarks to reporters on board:

I left my country exactly three and a half years ago. When I last met with the American President, it was merely a farewell greeting and there was no special statement entrusted. I only heard about the formation of the Okada cabinet the day before I arrived in Honolulu. I was asked many questions by reporters in Honolulu, and I tried my best to explain that Japan's foreign policy would not change due to the change of the cabinet. Foreign Minister Hirota's criticisms in the United States are very good. Compared with my time as acting ambassador last year, American sentiment towards Japan has greatly improved. Regarding the Hirota-Hull exchange of letters, Secretary Hull originally intended to include more meaning in them, but that document seems to have had a great impact and can be regarded as the cornerstone of Japanese-American diplomatic relations, even if it is a laughing matter. Secondly, looking at the United States' attitude towards the disarmament conference, it seems that only its naval authorities have drawn up a draft, and it has not yet consulted with the State Department on its formal plan. As for the national relations between Japan and the United States, the Hirota-Hull exchange of letters is already sufficient. Treaties of non-aggression and non-war are really unnecessary.

Furthermore, after a short stay in Tokyo, the ambassador plans to inspect "Manchukuo," and his return to the United States can be expected by October. (Japan United Press dispatch, 17th)

Japan's Policy on Naval Conference Prepares to Tear Up Treaty: Notification Date to be Determined Based on Conference Situation 65

(Tokyo) At yesterday's meeting of the highest naval leadership at the Naval Minister's residence, all strongly advocated withdrawal from unfavorable existing treaties as one of the fundamental policies of the Japanese Navy for the disarmament conference. However, according to this principle, the denunciation of the Washington Treaty must be notified before the end of December this year, the date on which its warning period expires. However, the Foreign Ministry believes that if the preparatory naval talks to be reopened in October do not achieve the expected results, or if the main conference has no hope of concluding a new treaty, it will not be too late to notify at that time. This view is not final. If there is a need for immediate notification, the Foreign Ministry will begin diplomatic work with England, America, and France, and then adopt decisive diplomatic measures. (Dentsu dispatch, 17th)

Japanese Army and Navy Vice Ministers Retained 66

(Tokyo) Army Vice Minister Toki Akira, Viscount (Research), Army Advisor Ishii Saburo (Seiyukai), and Navy Vice Minister Hotta Masatsune, Count (Research), and Navy Advisor Kawashima Masajiro have all been decided to retain their positions. (Dentsu Dispatch, 17th)

Germany Expresses Objections to Eastern European Pact 67

(London) The British government recently formally notified Germany and Poland that Britain supports the joint conclusion of a regional mutual assistance pact by Germany, the Soviet Union, the Baltic states, Poland, Czechoslovakia, etc. Although the firm replies from the German and Polish governments have not yet been sent to London, it is generally believed that after the British ambassadors to Germany and Poland spoke separately on the previous two days, the British government has obtained more accurate information regarding the reservations raised by the German and Polish governments, especially the German government. According to Berlin, when British Ambassador to Germany Phipps first visited Foreign Minister Neurath last Friday, the German Foreign Minister had already raised some objections in his personal capacity. Phipps visited again the day before yesterday, and it is said that Neurath reiterated the objections he had expressed last time and raised a question, namely, whether de facto military equality is a prerequisite for Germany to join the mutual assistance pact, or whether it will be achieved after the pact is established. He urgently wants to know, but as far as Germany is concerned, it must follow the first method in order to support the mutual assistance pact. In addition, the German Foreign Minister also inquired about the extent to which Germany would be allowed to reorganize its army in order to conform to de facto equality. Because the German side has this kind of demand, the British Cabinet Disarmament Committee believes that the matter is important and suddenly convened a meeting on Downing Street this morning to discuss countermeasures. As for Poland, the general public seems to express some doubts, fearing that the Soviet Union will benefit the most after the mutual assistance pact is established, and the relationship between Russia and France will be greatly improved, while Poland will inevitably be overshadowed. Polish people also have doubts about the validity of the Soviet Union's guarantee. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

British Officer Shot Near Samos Island: Disobeyed Stop Order: Turkish Sentry Mistakenly Opened Fire: Turkish Government Apologizes to England 71

The other day, Lieutenant Commander Robinson and Lieutenant Commander Monsell were sailing when they were shot by a Turkish sentry opposite the island. Lieutenant Commander Robinson was shot and fell into the sea and went missing. Lieutenant Commander Monsell was slightly injured. The Turkish bulletin stated that a Turkish customs officer saw three naked men landing on the beach from a sailboat and ordered them to stop, but they ignored him. The Turkish government has instructed the Turkish ambassador in London to apologize to the British government. Lieutenant Commander Robinson's body has not yet been recovered. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

Hungarian Government Dissolves Illegal Groups 73

After the San Francisco General Strike Began, the Prosperous City Became a Ghost Town

Riots Erupted Yesterday, Descending into Chaos: The Garrison Army Surrounded the Strike Area as if Facing a Formidable Enemy: All Industries Shut Down, with a Trend of Spreading to the Atlantic Coast 74

After the San Francisco general strike began, the garrison here increased to 4,000 people, 2,000 of whom marched through the city. In addition to carrying machine guns, tanks equipped with one-pound cannons were also deployed, as if facing a formidable enemy. The provincial authorities also ordered the 160th Garrison Infantry of Los Angeles to surround the strike area. The team immediately carried 75mm cannons and headed to the strike area. Now traffic in San Francisco is completely cut off, and the bustling city has instantly turned into a ghost town. (United Press Dispatch, 17th)

(New York) It was learned today that transportation workers on the Atlantic coast also have a tendency to respond to the dockworkers on the Pacific coast and go on strike. Government authorities and transportation companies are doing their best to avoid this danger and prevent the complete halt of foreign trade in the United States. (National Telegraph, 16th)

According to New York newspapers regarding San Francisco, New York sailors will not stage a sympathy strike because their contracts are not due to expire until the end of September, and their leaders have stated that they will abide by the contracts. Almost all of California's seven National Guard units are now concentrated here. In addition, 2,600 more people arrived here at night, bringing five Walter tanks and machine gun and artillery units. After the troops arrived, they immediately built obstacles, and especially paid attention to the agricultural areas south of the city. All vehicles carrying food into the city are escorted by military police. Mayor Rossi declared that he had no intention of declaring martial law, and Washington officials also denied that local officials had formally requested help from the central army. Cities in the East Bay such as Oakland, Berkeley, and Alameda joined the general strike today. The Governor of California has reported this matter to President Roosevelt and discussed solutions with him. (Reuters dispatch, 17th)

The San Francisco general strike began this morning, aiming to bring the entire territory of San Francisco, with a population of 1.3 million, to a standstill. The strikers are rushing to implement their plan, wanting to have the same strike in Portland, Oregon.

Riots Erupt 75

After the strike was realized here, riots broke out. 1,500 people robbed grocery stores, and a mob of about 50 people broke into the San Francisco Communist Party headquarters, moved out its equipment and set it on fire. Disturbances also occurred in Oakland, across from San Francisco. Police and rioters clashed, causing a lot of material damage, with several people injured on both sides. It is estimated that no less than 150,000 people are on strike, but the authorities are now taking various methods to prevent their actions from going off track. This is extremely difficult.

Troop Deployment 76

This morning, tanks carrying small cannons and machine guns rushed to San Francisco. The artillery unit has been dispatched, and 1,000 National Guardsmen have arrived here by special train from Los Angeles.

All Industries Halt 77

All industries throughout the city have stopped, streetcars have stopped, and only private vehicles travel on the road. The police are all double-posted to prevent attacks. An official from the dockworkers' union told a Reuters reporter that the workers were confident of victory and did not want any riots. In the past three days, the cost of riot insurance has tripled and is still rising, indicating the seriousness of the situation. A general strike has been proposed for Alabama yarn mills, and a truck drivers' strike will begin in Minneapolis tonight.

Prices Skyrocket 78

The labor unrest in San Francisco has caused prices to soar. Ham has jumped up by 12 cents per pound, and the price of cakes has tripled. The price of milk and butter is especially high. A few restaurants that have not yet closed have many people waiting outside, hoping to be seated in turn. Hotels now use paper for towels instead of cloth to avoid washing. The Central Food Commission issued a statement to reassure residents that there is no shortage of food, as wholesalers in the city have food worth 10 million yuan in stock.

Elaborate Arrangements 79

The strikers have arranged their plans very carefully and have established 19 supply stations where workers and their families can purchase the food they need. Among the workers in San Francisco who were forced to strike, there were 850 streetcar drivers. It is unfortunate that they have lost their right to receive pensions upon retirement due to joining the strike.

Increased Police Force 80

This morning, the police chief recruited veterans to supplement the 200 special police force. California Governor Merriam gave a speech to the veterans, saying, "When you were called to service, I knew you would be able to answer the call and serve the state, just like you did for the country in the past."

Government Concern 81

Washington officials are closely watching the situation here. Telegrams between San Francisco and Washington are endless, and wireless and wire personnel are working very hard. Secretary of Labor Perkins stated that she hopes the Labor Mediation Council can discuss solutions. President Roosevelt is currently traveling abroad and has not yet indicated that he will return to the United States immediately, although he has received various reports of developments.

Food Supplies at Risk 82

The food supply problem in San Francisco has indeed become acute. Fresh meat is no longer available, and supplies are now running out. Hundreds of restaurants have closed, and the rest may soon close down as well. It is expected that milk will be delivered as usual, but bread and other items may be stopped. Stores limit the sale of sugar and eggs. The 18 restaurants designated by the strikers will remain open, so residents in the most commercial areas may not have to worry about going hungry.

London's Footsteps 83

Today's state of San Francisco is reminiscent of the London general strike of 1926. A Reuters reporter drove out in his last gallon of gasoline to inspect everything. Employees of various offices, without transportation, walked on foot, carrying sandwiches, and rushing to their offices, still happy. Although there were many pedestrians on the street, the usual sound of cars was silent. The East Bay Strike Committee has now decided to allow shops to pick fresh fruits and vegetables before Tuesday for resale, and will allow gasoline to merchants to transport supplies to the shops. This decision is good news in the strike. (Reuters Dispatch, 16th)

More Than 100,000 People Participate in the Strike: An Unprecedented Initiative in American Labor History 84

The San Francisco Labor Council's strike guidance committee expressed its sympathy for the strike of Pacific coast dockworkers and decided to carry out a general strike. Despite various mediations by the authorities, it was ineffective, and the general strike began at 8:00 a.m. on the 16th (12:00 a.m. on the 16th, China time). 144 groups here participated in the strike, with a total of 65,000 people. Before the general strike, dockworkers, truckers, interior decorators, clerks, laundry workers, and streetcar workers, totaling 42,800 people, had already started the strike, totaling 106,800 people. This is an unprecedented major strike in American labor history. (Japan United Press dispatch, 16th)

Government Takes a Non-Interference Attitude 85

(Washington) The government continues to take a non-interference attitude towards the general strike in San Francisco and the labor movement on the Pacific coast. According to the White House, President Roosevelt has no intention of landing in San Francisco to personally interfere. The Labor Department and the newly established National Labor Relations Board, although assisting the mediators appointed by the President, are also strictly neutral. This afternoon, the Labor Relations Board announced that it had sent Schoedonog to San Francisco for investigation. The Labor Department also stated that its mediator, Myers, will go to California, but these two have no other independent task other than to cooperate with the original mediator as much as possible. It is heard that Reconstruction Administration Director Johnson has flown from Portland to San Francisco to help resolve the labor unrest. The military has ordered the troops stationed in San Francisco not to take leave, but said that the movement of regular troops to curb the general strike has not been considered. Officials here received a telegram from San Francisco labor leaders saying that there is no danger of the people of San Francisco being hungry, so they don’t seem very panic. (National Telegraph, 16th)

Northwest Blockade Causes Shocking Losses 86

Seattle The labor movement on the Pacific Northwest coast is becoming more tense today and can be said to have reached the final decisive battle. Although there is no disturbance in Seattle, the workers are all ready to act. It is found that Seattle also had a general strike in 1919, the result of which was very bad. Since the San Francisco dockworkers' strike, it has been greatly affected since May. As for the situation in Portland, according to the news obtained here by the labor community, it will soon respond to San Francisco and implement a general strike. At present, although there is no general strike in other places besides San Francisco, the losses are shocking if the northwest coast is blocked for a long time. For example, logging, one of the main industries here, has now completely stopped, and thousands of workers are idle all day long. As for wheat, due to the drought in the west, there is a very severe shortage. Although it has been harvested here, it cannot be transported. Fresh fruits worth about 3 million yuan will spoil because they cannot be transported. Wool is also piled up in warehouses, waiting for prices to skyrocket. Gasoline in the Northwest is becoming increasingly scarce, and farmers need a lot of oil, so they are also greatly damaged. (National Telegraph, 16th)

Strike Leaders Reassure the Public: Fear of Losing Sympathy 87

Since the San Francisco general strike has begun, the leaders, in view of the reason for the failure of the 1919 general strike being the loss of public sympathy, intend to require workers serving in public transportation agencies to resume work as a precautionary measure. This request was initiated by the Strike Strategy Committee, which is composed of 25 representatives selected from the Central Strike Committee. During the recent labor unrest, they have full authority to decide on any measures. Today, the chairman of the committee issued a resolution, expressing gratitude for the enthusiastic assistance of the transportation workers, and at the same time requesting that they immediately resume work. The general public regards this resolution as sufficient proof of the intention of the strike committee, which is not to disrupt urban life too much, so as not to lose the sympathy of the general public. However, the 2,500 employees of transportation agencies in San Francisco and Oakland are determined and continue to strike despite the above request. (Havas dispatch, 16th)

San Francisco strike leaders are cool-headed, and the stagnant situation here has loosened, and the tense atmosphere has eased. The news of riots received is not of a major nature. In order to win public sympathy and avoid bloodshed, the General Strike Committee has announced that it will never let people go hungry and ordered the highway pickets not to interfere with vehicles carrying food. Therefore, one of the greatest fears of the people has now been dispelled. The committee also expressed its opinion that it would allow more restaurants to operate as usual and notified streetcar workers to return to work. The post office announced today that mail will be collected and delivered as usual. At the same time, according to a Reuters dispatch from Washington, the government has entrusted the matter of mediating labor disputes to three mediators, namely, the Director of the National Labor Bureau, Wagner, negotiator Donohue, and Labor Department official Myers. All three of them have set off for San Francisco today. Newspapers in the strike area all say that the general strike was instigated by the Communist Party and predict that the strike will not achieve any results. (Reuters Dispatch, 17th)

Church Prayer for Industrial Peace 88

In San Francisco, where the labor unrest persists and human efforts have failed to resolve it, churches have widely opened for prayer meetings, seeking the benevolence of Heaven to restore industrial peace. However, the general strike commenced this morning at 8 AM, and is rapidly spreading. Café waiters and barbers, along with five hundred wireless radio operators, have joined the strike. The only ones who have not joined are the letterpress printers. The cessation of work by wireless radio operators is extremely significant to the shipping industry. According to federal law, passenger ships cannot sail without licensed wireless radio operators. As most of them are union members, they have no choice but to obey the union's orders. Streetcars and cargo trucks in the city have completely ceased operation. The National Guard has been increased to four thousand men. Violent acts are escalating in the East Bay area of San Francisco. Several cargo trucks loaded with food have been pushed into nearby ditches by strike pickets. Currently, officials are recruiting special police in Oakland, Berkeley, and Alameda to bolster the police force. (Havas Dispatch, 16th)

Anecdotes from the Midst of the Strike 89

The general strike in San Francisco is not without its interesting anecdotes. The demand for roller skates has suddenly surged. Today, a young woman insisted on buying a pair, saying she would skate through the streets to her workplace. Rooftops are crowded with onlookers watching tanks moving back and forth, the distribution of machine guns, and the patrol of seven thousand National Guard troops. Four streetcars, driven by non-strikers and protected by armed police, are running on the tracks. Officials are making every effort to maintain order in the city. (Reuters Dispatch, 17th)

Setback for High Altitude Expedition: Team Members Missing or Fallen 90

News has arrived of a major setback for the German Himalayan expedition led by Simula. Three key members of the expedition—Merkel, Wieland, and Wienbut—have been missing for three days, while three worker porters have died in a snowstorm. The expedition had reached an altitude of 23,000 feet in the Himalayas when they encountered the storm. Team members were disoriented and scattered. After the storm subsided somewhat, they had to halt their advance and begin searching for the missing members. (National Dispatch, 17th)

Mount Aso in Japan Erupts, Spewing Rocks 91

(Tokyo) Mount Aso, which had been rumbling continuously since last night, erupted violently at 10:20 AM today, with an extremely intense eruption of volcanic ash. Approximately three hundred soldiers from the Combined Fleet and over one hundred general climbers who were on the mountain at the time immediately took refuge in mountain temples. So far, there have been no reports of injuries to people or animals. (Den-tsu Dispatch, 17th)

Japanese Preparations for Attacking Soviet Russia: Forced Conscription in Southern Fengtian Province and Expansion of Plans to Invade Inner Mongolia 92

Shenyang Special Dispatch: The Japanese military authorities recently compelled the puppet government to implement conscription, starting in the southern part of puppet Fengtian Province. Villages are divided into three categories—A, B, and C—to determine the conscription quota. Category A villages, with over one hundred households, must provide eighty recruits; Category B villages, with over fifty households, must provide forty recruits; and Category C villages, with over twenty households, must provide twenty recruits. The conscription is based on one recruit per household. After conscription, all recruits are trained by Japanese instructors attached to the puppet gendarmerie headquarters. The Japanese are using this aggressive conscription method to prepare for a war with Russia. Currently, conscription has begun in Liaoyang, Liaozhong, Shenyang, and Xinmin counties. Recently, eighty young men were conscripted from Qianhutun village in southern Shenyang. The men, women, old, and young family members of the conscripted wept loudly, seeing them off with heartbreaking cries for over ten miles. The scene was unbearable to witness.

Changchun Special Dispatch: In order to expedite plans to attack Soviet Russia, the Japanese are expanding their plan to invade Inner Mongolia. Recently, the Japanese General Staff selected junior officers and soldiers from various divisions who are proficient in Chinese and familiar with the situation in the country, forming a brigade to participate in incitement work in Inner Mongolia. Simultaneously, ten airfields are being constructed in Liaoning, thirteen in Jilin, ten in Heilongjiang, and seven in Jehol as preparations for defense against Russia. These airfields were completed recently. (Northeast News Agency)

The Panchen Lama's Return to Tibet: Will Travel to Qinghai via the Yikezhao League to Prepare for Return; Huang Musong Enters Tibet to Reconcile Factions 93

Beiping Correspondence: The Panchen Erdeni arrived in Beiping by plane yesterday (the 14th). After disembarking, he went directly to Fengze Garden in Zhonghai to rest. This morning (the 15th), the Panchen Lama issued the following statement: "I will stay in Beiping for about ten days. Currently, transportation on the Ping-Sui Railway is inconvenient due to the flooding in Pingdiquan. The train only goes to Pingdiquan, as the station was washed away. I will go to the Yikezhao League to chant scriptures after the flood subsides. I have decided to chant scriptures for a month. Regarding the issue of returning to Tibet, I met with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in Nanjing, and all procedures have been agreed upon, but I cannot disclose them. There are also solutions to various issues concerning Tibetan internal affairs, diplomacy, religion, and education. The Central Government is extremely concerned about Tibet, so they instructed me to return. The main purpose of my return is to convey the Central Government's intentions to Tibet, so that there is no separation between Tibet and the Central Government, and between the Central Government and Tibet. The first step of my return route is to go to Qinghai via the Yikezhao League. I will stay in Qinghai for a considerable period. After Mr. Huang Musong enters Tibet, I will assess the actual situation and then decide the date of my return. Second, various preparations must be made for the return. The preparations will be finalized in Qinghai. Mr. Huang Musong often sends telegrams to me, and he is expected to arrive in Lhasa next month. As for the rumors that I will go to Bailing Temple, they are completely false. The youth opposition to autonomy is not a problem. I will not go to Bailing Temple because there is nothing for me to do there. If necessary, I will pray for rain while I am in Beiping. When I was in Nanjing, I went to Qixia Mountain to pray for rain, and it rained for two hours as a result. I will find a way to irrigate the drought-stricken counties of He and Luo. The only way is to pray for rain," and so on.

The Panchen Lama's bodyguard of one hundred and fifty men will arrive in Beiping tomorrow (the 16th). One of the bodyguards died of heatstroke in Nanjing. These one hundred-odd bodyguards will accompany the Panchen Lama when he goes to the Yikezhao League. The difficulty of returning to Tibet lies in the different attitudes of the Tibetan side towards welcoming or rejecting the Panchen Lama. Most lamas in the rear of Tibet welcome the Panchen Lama's return to the west, while the youth in the front of Tibet reject his return because of ideological differences. It is said that Huang Musong's entry into Tibet is to reconcile the opinions of the two factions. (15th)

Rivers in Hebei Province Overflow 丨 Yongding River Breaches 丨 97

Tianjin Correspondence: In recent weeks, heavy rainfall has occurred frequently in northern Hebei, causing all rivers and canals to fill up and overflow. The Provincial Construction Department has received reports of rising water levels in various rivers, except for the Yellow River, including the Daqing River, Zhulong River, Southern Grand Canal, Northern Grand Canal, Luan River, and Huanxiang River. Yutian County, in the third and fourth districts, reported flooding from the Huanxiang River, inundating over 40 villages and destroying over a thousand acres of crops. The Wei River, a tributary of the Northern Grand Canal, overflowed on the night of the 13th, flooding five villages east of Tianjin, including Yixingbu, Yangcun, and Huojiazicun. Residents fled to rooftops in the middle of the night, and countless livestock drowned. The 60 li stretch from Tianjin to Yangcun is a vast expanse of water, impassable by boat. The Yongding River's surge is particularly severe. Since the 7th of this month, the water level has reached over the bridges at Lugouqiao and Jianbaqiao, reaching a maximum of 63.38 meters. The upstream sections near Wen'an and Ba County are level with the banks, posing a critical threat. Men Zhenzhong, Director of the Yongding River Affairs Bureau, repeatedly telegraphed the Construction Department and the Yongding River Engineering Committee, requesting urgent funds for rescue to prevent flooding in the Wen'an and Ba County areas. In addition to instructing the River Affairs Bureau to take careful precautions, the Construction Department dispatched a commissioner with the remaining 29,000 yuan from the spring flood prevention funds to expedite flood control. Due to the rising river levels, the Construction Department ordered the staff of the Second Section, Dispatch Department, and Secretariat to work in shifts to avoid delays. On the night of the 13th, the Yongding River suddenly breached upstream. Dozens of villages near Qiajiadian were flooded with four to five feet of water. The flood was vast. The area, together with the Northern Grand Canal, has become a watery expanse. Over 4,000 acres of farmland were destroyed, and the flood continues to rise. The area is expected to be submerged further. The cause of the breach is that the Hai River Conservancy Commission, due to the heavy silt content of the Yongding River, which often causes problems for the Hai River during floods, diverted the river at Qiajiadian, above Beicang, to the low-lying areas north of Sanjiaodian, and built a control mechanism near Qiajiadian to regulate the flow. Recently, the flood overflowed in the Yubakou area north of Sanjiaodian, causing Xianzhuang, Dongxiaozhuang, and the Dingzhuang villages to become a watery expanse. At 5:00 PM on the 13th, villagers from Wangqinzhuang gathered at the control mechanism, demanding that the gatekeeper open the control gate to allow for drainage. The gatekeeper refused, and the villagers left dissatisfied. At midnight, a group of several hundred people gathered and destroyed the mouth of the old river channel. The local security team arrived after receiving the news, but it was too late. The dike collapsed, and the flood returned to the old channel, entering the Grand Canal. The Northern Grand Canal could not contain the water, and it overflowed onto the banks. Over fifty villages in the surrounding area were flooded. The flood was vast. The Hai River Conservancy Commission and the Construction Department's commissioner went to inspect the area today. Seeing that there was no way to prevent the flood, they decided to guide the river into the Grand Canal to mitigate the flood in the nearby area. The residents of the flooded areas are living on rooftops, and the Charity Association is rushing to provide relief. (14th)

Yongxin After Recovery: Former Specialties Generated Tens of Millions in Revenue; Population Loss Exceeded Hundreds of Thousands After the Calamity; Active Efforts Being Made in Rural Clearance and Post-Disaster Relief 98

Nanchang Correspondence: Yongxin County in western Jiangxi was formerly the lair of the Xiao bandits. After its recovery, it became a pivotal point for the National Army's suppression of bandits. Such is its importance. The area was recovered by the Western Route Army's Wang Dongyuan Division in January of this year. However, after years of devastation, it is difficult to restore its vitality. According to the on-site survey by the Western Route Headquarters' Yifu Brigade, the following is a summary:

Local Situation 99

Yongxin is located on the west bank of the Gan River, bordering Ji'an and Taihe to the east, Chaling, Hunan, to the west, Ninggang and Suichuan to the south, Lianhua to the northwest, and Anfu to the northeast. Although it is located in a remote border area, its water and land transportation is quite convenient. The He River originates from He Mountain, connecting to Lianhua upstream and reaching Ji'an downstream. In the past, boats traveled frequently, with sails like walls. The Badu River can also accommodate small boats and rafts, allowing for unimpeded transportation. The border area is surrounded by mountains. Yi Mountain in the east and Tian'eling in Taihe are remotely connected. He Mountain and Meihua Mountain in the west serve as the natural border with Chaling. In the south, Huangzhulun is connected to Qixilun in Ninggang. Shen Mountain and Xuhuang Mountain in the north are naturally steep, resembling another world. Therefore, the communist bandits occupied it as a nest for five or six years. Although it has been recovered by the National Army for several months, the area is exhausted, and the people are demoralized, awaiting active post-disaster relief.

After the Calamity 100

Before Yongxin fell into the hands of the bandits, Xiaojiangshan, Badushan, Luofushan, and other places produced tens of thousands of dollars worth of timber annually. The mines in Tianhe and the iron factory boilers were worth millions of dollars annually. The lime from Shihuibiao to Shihui was a famous specialty. In total, the annual revenue reached tens of millions of dollars. As a result, commerce was prosperous, and schools were numerous. There were two middle schools, Hechuan and Vocational, five complete primary schools, and over two hundred elementary schools. The customs and sentiments of the people were slightly different from those in other places. Generally, the eastern villages were honest, the southern villages were lewd, the northern villages were simple and honest, and the western villages were strong and cunning. This is due to the formation of mountains and plains. The love of writing and vanity became common customs. Therefore, before communization, men of letters rose up. Since Zhu De and Mao Zedong sneaked into Jinggang Mountain in the 18th year of the Republic of China, they occupied it as a base and actively developed towards Yongxin, Ninggang, Lianhua, Chaling, Yixian, Exian, and Suichuan counties. The government's reach was too limited, so a spark turned into a prairie fire.

Extent of Damage 101

According to the statistics compiled by the county in the 17th year of the Republic of China, there were a total of 375,400 people. After falling into the hands of the bandits, approximately 50,000 to 60,000 people were killed by the communist bandits under the names of local bullies, corrupt officials, intellectuals, and reactionaries. No less than 30,000 people fled elsewhere. About 10,000 people died in other villages due to famine, disease, and epidemics. About 4,000 to 5,000 Yongxin refugees were killed after the fall of Ji'an. Approximately 10,000 people were killed after the bandits under the name of AB Corps. In total, the county lost more than 100,000 people. Over 5,000 buildings were burned down. There are no accurate statistics on property loss. At present, the ruins and debris are desolate, and the land is like an ancient battlefield. Recalling the scenes of the past, the descendants of Yongxin will never forget the Communist Party.

Rural Clearance and Post-Disaster Relief 102

When the Western Route Army recovered the county, it immediately ordered the organization of a Rural Clearance and Post-Disaster Relief Committee to handle various post-disaster relief efforts. The members of the committee were recommended by the Yongxin Fellow Villagers Association in the province to return and take charge. Their work is considered to be diligent. The first step was to handle surrenders and new beginnings. As of the end of June, 448 people from the eastern villages, 245 from the southern villages, 180 from the western villages, and 147 from the northern villages had registered. 497 certificates of new beginnings were issued. The second step was to organize pao and shen. 26 pao have been organized in the first district, 6 pao in the third district, over 30 pao in the fourth district, over 38 pao in the fifth district, and over 30 pao in the sixth district. The second and seventh districts have not been fully recovered. About 8,000 refugees fled, of whom over 420 have been accommodated. 600 refugees have been accommodated in the Litian Refugee Shelter. There have been 600-700 surrenders and captives. Since the recovery, the Jiangxi Provincial Relief Association has distributed over 20,000 yuan in relief funds, and the Western Route Army has distributed over 5,000 yuan. However, after the great devastation, a drop in the bucket is still difficult to provide universal relief.

Water Level Recedes in the Lower Reaches of the Yellow River in Shandong; Gongjia Turns from Danger to Safety 103

Jitong Correspondence: Several days ago, the water level in the upper reaches of the Yellow River suddenly rose and flowed downstream. The river water within the province also increased by more than one meter, flowing rapidly. Gongjia, in the jurisdiction of Lijin County in the lower reaches of the province, has always been known as a dangerous section of the river. When the water level was at its highest the other day, a river beach collapsed violently, reaching the base of the levee. County Magistrate Ye Yunbiao immediately telegraphed the provincial government to report the situation. The provincial government ordered the River Affairs Bureau to quickly supervise the construction and rescue work. The River Affairs Bureau immediately ordered Liang Jinming, the chief of the downstream section, to personally inspect and supervise the repairs. Liang arrived at Gongjia on the 14th with Zhao Rongfu, who was responsible for the defense. Because the water level had receded and the collapse of the river beach had slowed down, the situation stabilized. In addition to ordering the section chief to continue throwing stones to protect the area, he requested that more sacks be issued for use. The River Affairs Bureau has already issued another 3,000 sacks. 400 of the 500 cubic meters of stone that were originally prepared have already been transported. Liang Jinming has been ordered not to return to Qinghe and to temporarily supervise the construction at Gongjia. The dangerous section should be safe. The provincial government ordered each county along the Yellow River to build a shelter every li on the levee, each shelter accommodating five people, to be reported by a deadline. This is to prepare for a major flood in the future, so that if there are not enough river defense soldiers, civilian laborers can be added to help, living in the shelters to avoid the wind and rain. The following is the telegram from Liang Jinming: "Zhang Junjian, Director of the Jinan River Affairs Bureau, Liang Jinming and others arrived at Gongjia this afternoon to inspect the dangerous section. Due to the strong water flow in the past few days, the river beach collapsed rapidly. The upper and middle sections now have a remaining width of seven to two or three zhang, and the narrowest head in the lower section has only eight or nine chi. Many hanging willows have been washed away. They are now being replanted. Fortunately, the water level has dropped significantly since yesterday, and the collapse has slowed down. The situation has stabilized. The stone material has been inspected and accepted by Councilor Ge. The section chief has been ordered to first load and throw sacks at the bottom of the lower section, and then use stone to protect it, so that it can be effective quickly. However, the sacks issued are not enough. Please issue 6,000 sacks to meet the urgent need. In addition, I met with the County Magistrate of Lijin at Gongjia to discuss the construction work, etc. He has agreed to send 200 people to help load the sacks. I plan to return to Qinghe tomorrow and report this by telegram. Liang Jinming bows his head." (16th)

Review of Garrison Troops in Various Regions: Entire Area Divided into Twelve Districts; Deadline for Review is the 25th 104

Taiyuan Correspondence: The Shanxi-Suiyuan Military Reorganization Committee, in order to rectify military discipline and assess the academic and technical performance of various units, as well as the downsizing situation, has specifically decided to start the third year, second phase review and supervision training on the 15th of this month, with a deadline of the 25th. The Military Reorganization Committee has drafted a review and supervision training plan and assigned a colonel section chief, nine major general supervising officers, and two major general advisors, each with an attendant soldier. They will depart separately today and tomorrow. The committee also believes that due to the road construction duties of the various units, the implementation of education varies. Therefore, while dispatching personnel to supervise the review, they will also implement supervision training. The review and supervision training subjects will be in accordance with the scheduled review subjects of each unit, divided into academic subjects, technical subjects, and internal affairs, for detailed inspection. Special attention will be paid to military discipline. Units engaged in road construction and land reclamation are exempt from this review, but the supervision training of units engaged in road construction will focus on the current work situation, education level, and the quality of military discipline, and will be assessed in detail. Each regiment is expected to complete the supervision training in two days. The review and supervision training is divided into nine groups of infantry, one group of cavalry, and two groups of artillery, totaling twelve groups, according to the number of troops. (13th)

Clearing of Bandits on the Jiangxi-Anhui Border Imminent: Loss of Base After Recovery of Yingxi 105

Wuyuan Correspondence: The bandit gangs that have been disturbing the border between Qimen and Fuliang have been defeated by the joint attack and suppression of Chen Tiaoyuan's two battalions led by Li Tuan and Jiao Qu, and Liu Commissioner Xiao Xiu's district ten security brigade in Anhui Province. The remaining bandits fled to the Chengjiashan and Yingxi areas, attempting a final struggle. Recently, Jiao Battalion launched a fierce offensive, and Yingxi has been recovered. Over fifty bandits have been killed. With the loss of their new base, the bandits have been unable to succeed and have scattered. The Jingzhen Campaign Headquarters' Special Operations Detachment recently led the security regiments to enter and suppress the bandit lairs in Xinqiao, Jiaotan, Zhongshan, Songshukeng, and other places in Fuliang County, capturing over twenty people, including Tao Guangming, the chairman of the puppet Su District, and Zhang Huigang, the puppet regiment commander, and seizing a large number of rifles and school badges. In addition, over two hundred bandits in Liujiawan, Ezipao, and other places, over thirty li from Jingzhen, were severely suppressed by Zhang Battalion of the 55th Division and fled without a trace. Li Leifu, the deputy commander of the Jiangxi-Anhui border area stationed in Jingde by the Campaign Headquarters, arrived in Zhen with a battalion of guards and has contacted the various units, actively surrounding and suppressing the bandits. With attacks from all sides, it is difficult for the bandits to rise again. As for the scattered bandits in western Wuyuan, County Magistrate Liu personally led a team to clear the rural areas, uncovering several bandit nests. The coerced people have surrendered one after another. The large towns in the fifth district of the township, including Fuchun, Chongtian, Jiadao, Yanqian, Changxi, and Yantian, have been urged by District Chief Tan to organize civil corps to implement self-defense. The bandit forces will not grow stronger. With the advance and encirclement of the various bandit suppression troops, it is expected that they can be wiped out in the shortest possible time. (12th)

Nanchang Discovers Blood-Touching Gang, Inspector Assaulted for Advising Against Bare Chest, Authorities Order Strict Investigation and Arrest 106

Nanchang Dispatch: Zhang Ke, an inspector of the Public Security Bureau of the Jiangxi provincial capital, was patrolling Desheng Road the other day when he saw a man with a bare chest. Given the strict ban against going shirtless, he stepped forward to advise him. Unexpectedly, the man remained calm and lightly touched Inspector Zhang's right flank. At first, Inspector Zhang was unaware, only feeling a slight chill. Later, while patrolling Zhongshan Road, he felt numbness and pain in his right flank. Zhang, skilled in martial arts and with some knowledge of bone-setting medicine, suspected something was amiss. He went to a famous bone-setter for treatment, who, after manipulation, caused him to vomit several mouthfuls of black blood, slightly alleviating his injury. Yesterday, Zhang reported the situation to Inspector Hua, who relayed it to the bureau chief. After hearing the report, Director Huang, considering the insidious harm of blood-touching injuries to society and the unwarranted assault on a police officer as extremely audacious, ordered all branch bureaus and detective teams to conduct a strict investigation and arrest to deter future incidents. (July 16)

Songjiang: Detailed Account of the Destruction of Songhui Amusement Park 107

Songjiang has long lacked entertainment venues. Since the completion of the Songhui Road automobile road in past years, landowners with property along the road have built commercial houses in hopes of developing the market. Most notably, the Songjiang Dayue Theater was opened, showing movies and Peking opera, enjoying a prosperous business. Subsequently, Yin Shisheng, the manager of the automobile company, added buildings to the Songhui Xiaozhu, where cars were parked, decorating it with pavilions, terraces, and ponds. Part of it was used as his own residence, while the rest was developed into Songhui Amusement Park, featuring Shanghai opera, "four-hoang" opera, spoken drama, movies, and other variety acts for public entertainment. Tickets were priced at 320 wen. His wife, Shi Yaxiong, managed the operation. After its opening, citizens favored the park's open space as a place to cool off in the summer, attracting large crowds. However, Shi's supervision of ticket collection required even children brought by visitors to have tickets, and on Saturday nights, the park doubled its prices for fireworks performances, inevitably causing resentment among visitors. The brick-throwing that damaged the gate lights the other night was reportedly due to this. The First District Fire Brigade, at the park's opening, sent representatives to negotiate monthly donations, but Yin and Shi refused to acknowledge local donations. Despite the mediation of Yuan Da Silk's Jiang Zhucheng and Cheng Shujun, no agreement was reached. Members of the Songjiang Fire Brigade are all store employees who volunteer their services and work hard to put out fires. They gradually raise funds to replace fire-fighting equipment with pumps to increase efficiency. Regular expenses rely on monthly donations from shops and residents. Amusement parks are closely related to the fire brigade. Songjiang Grand Theater acknowledges monthly donations, but only Songhui Amusement Park refuses to donate. Therefore, the Fire Brigade announced it would gather every night on Songhui Road to test drive fire engines. The Yin family viewed this as a demonstration. On the evening of the 12th, when visitors were throwing bricks and damaging the park's doors and windows, three people were arrested by the police. The next morning, news of the incident appeared in the newspaper, provoking widespread indignation among the Fire Brigade. The Fire Brigade investigated the person who submitted the article, and visited the county magistrate to inquire if he had said the Fire Brigade had some kind of backing, but no information was obtained. Yesterday, the county magistrate invited representatives from the county government, various legal groups, and the Fire Brigade to discuss a resolution, and decided to suspend the test drives for two days to peacefully resolve the issue. The Fire Brigade agreed to accept this. According to a declaration issued by the Fire Brigade, the county magistrate was biased towards the Yin family and was undermining the Fire Brigade. They telegraphed the provincial chairman and the director of civil affairs, and telegraphed fire brigades in other cities to provide unanimous support. Last night, while the Fire Brigade was holding an emergency meeting, a report came that a tourist's head was injured by a flying stone at Songhui Amusement Park, triggering public outrage. The crowd rushed into the park, smashing doors, windows, equipment, and some cabinets in Manager Yin's residence. They then piled rattan chairs in the yard and set them on fire. The Fire Brigade immediately drove to the scene to put out the fire, and the county government also dispatched police to the scene to suppress the disturbance. Although the turmoil was temporarily brought to an end, the park suffered considerable losses. It is said that the county magistrate and the victim, Yin, have both reported to the province. The county chamber of commerce also telegraphed Chen, the provincial chairman in Zhenjiang, and Yu Wenyun, the director of civil affairs, stating that a dispute broke out at Songhui Amusement Park in Songjiang last night, and rioters took the opportunity to set a fire, which affected public safety and was a cause for concern. They requested that the county magistrate quickly maintain public order and handle the matter impartially, which would be fortunate for the region. The Songjiang County Chamber of Commerce respectfully announced. It is said that the owner of the park, Yin Shisheng, has filed a lawsuit with the prosecutor's office, listing more than ten defendants, but summons have not yet been issued. The dispute in this case may not be easily resolved in the short term.

Long-Awaited Light Rain Brings Joy 108

Our city has been suffering from a prolonged drought for nearly a month, exacerbated by record-breaking heat for the past sixty years. As a result, rivers have dried up, farmland has cracked, farmers are filled with worry, and rice prices have risen to 13 yuan and 6 jiao, affecting all industries to a great extent. Local communities have voluntarily stopped slaughtering animals and set up altars at the Dongyang Taoist Temple to pray for rain, which had just ended yesterday. At 9:00 AM today, dark clouds suddenly gathered, and there was a very light rain. Then, at 10:30 AM, there was more light rain, which turned into a downpour at 11:00 AM, but only lasted for ten minutes before stopping. In the afternoon, the heat felt even more intense.

Suzhou: Three Major Panics in Suzhou City 109

During this severe drought in Suzhou City, not only have drinking water and food for the people become major problems, but also the canal water has dried up, and manure boats cannot pass through, making it difficult for manure collectors to work. In areas such as Guanqian Street, Zilan Lane, Daotang Lane, Gushi Lane, and Lindun Road, manure has not been collected for as long as four or five days in the worst cases. Most people are dumping manure in nearby toilets, filling the city with pits and gullies, and urine is everywhere, which is a great impediment to sanitation. Residents have repeatedly requested the county government and the sanitation association to find a solution. Some people have suggested that the government take over the manure collection and have the sanitation association hire manure collectors to collect manure from each household, collecting manure fees, and using the income, after expenses, to fund sanitation in each district. As for the drinking water problem, the drought prevention committee is using water pumps to pump water into the city at Louqi Gate and other places, transporting it by boat to supply people's needs. They are also releasing water from private artesian wells and building dams at Panxie and Fengmen gates to divert water from outside the city into the city for irrigation of the fields within the city. Regarding the food problem, yesterday (the 17th), the drought prevention committee decided that the county government should inform the rice industry association and relay to each shop not to raise rice prices any further. The grain storage committee will handle the grain storage issue. It was also decided that a letter should be sent from the county party headquarters to the provincial party headquarters to publicly sell the goods seized from traitors and use the proceeds to help with the drought relief. The county chamber of commerce is scheduled to convene a meeting this morning (the 18th) with leaders from the power plant, the rice industry, the silk reeling industry, and the electrical materials industry to discuss various important issues.

Wuxi: Official-Civilian Cooperation in Famine Relief 110

Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, the Wuxi County Government held its 21st administrative meeting, chaired by County Magistrate Yan, which resolved: 1. Regarding drought relief matters, the situation is urgent, and funds should be withdrawn according to regulations. In addition to using the remaining funds from silkworm rearing incentives and the agricultural promotion institute's previous allocations, 3,000 yuan each should be allocated from the industry and construction items. 2. The Construction Bureau is to order one 16-inch diameter water pump, one 12-inch diameter water pump, and two 10-inch diameter water pumps, totaling 1,415 yuan. 3. Since water pump engines are out of stock in all factories, it was decided to rent them from steamships. 4. The temporary measures for drought relief, dam construction, water pumping, and field irrigation were approved. 5. 200 dan of mung bean seeds, 100 dan of red bean seeds, and 40 dan of buckwheat seeds are to be purchased and distributed to various districts for planting. 6. Regarding the rescue of the city's water system, it was decided to set up wooden gates at the West Gate and the East Gate and set up machinery to pump water, which will still be handled by the First District Office, using 500 yuan of the previous police expenses for hiring workers to clean up accumulated manure. Toilet owners will be notified to clear it out within a specified time. County Magistrate Yan also noted that the first item listed in the implementation rules for the Jiangsu Construction Department's measures for drawing water from rivers and lakes to relieve drought relief, included the Lubu Port station, located in the northwest of Jiangyin, drawing water from the Yangtze River, which only benefits the northwest of Jiangyin and the northeast of Wujin. However, the three mouths of the Yellow Mountain Port, Yellow Field Port, and Xia Port in Wuxi County, through which the Yangtze River flows to the county's rivers, were not included in the station establishment and water drawing, which seemed to provide insufficient support for the irrigation of farmland in the southeastern part of Jiangyin County and the northeastern part of Wuxi County. In particular, the Yellow Field Port, which connects to the Xicheng Canal, is most important to both Wuxi and Cheng counties. Yesterday, a special telegram was sent to the Construction Department requesting that a station be established at the Yellow Field Port to draw water to benefit farmland. Regarding the Lu River mouth waterway, it is expected to be dredged by today and the dam will be removed immediately. The river channels in Furong Wei and other places are being dredged by villagers voluntarily. At 3:00 PM on the 16th, dark clouds gathered and thunder rumbled, making all the residents of the city rejoice, but with a clap of thunder, the roof ridge of the house of Zou Dehou Tang's Zou Laotai in the South Gate was struck and destroyed, without any rain, which caused great disappointment. However, Zengting, Xintang Bridge, Luoshe, Outang Bridge, and Nanqiao all received inches of rain one after another, but it was still not enough to make a difference. It is also heard that the county government has budgeted drought relief funds up to 10,000 yuan. Wuxi resident Gong Haiqin and others yesterday submitted a request to the county party headquarters to restrict rice prices to maintain the livelihood of the poor and prevent a famine.

Xing Jingyao Commits Suicide in Hotel 111

Xinsutai Hotel on Mabian Road in our county, on the afternoon of the other day, a Shanghai traveler arrived, claiming to be Xing Jingyao, 30 years old. He immediately booked Room 14 on the second floor. That evening, he ordered the tea boy to mail a letter to a certain lady at the New China Hotel in Shanghai. It was not until 3:00 AM that he went to bed. However, until 10:00 AM yesterday, he had not gotten up. The tea boy was suspicious and pried open the door, only to find that Xing had stiffened on the bed, knowing that he had poisoned himself to death. He immediately reported to the front desk, who reported to Tu Zheng Xi Xuechang of the 13th Ward. The local branch sent prosecutor Shen to lead officials to inspect the scene. It was confirmed that he had committed suicide by taking opium. A diary and a letter from the Central Army Military Academy Training Class, Second Brigade, Sixteenth Team, signed Song Jieqian, were left behind and taken to the court for filing, awaiting relatives to claim the body.

Changshu: Large Number of Rice Boats Exported 112

The weather is severely dry, and rice prices have soared as a result. The price of white rice has suddenly risen in recent days to over 12 yuan, and coarse rice is also approaching 10 yuan, more than double what it was two months ago. Currently, the general populace is in a state of panic, and the authorities are trying to remedy the situation. According to news from Fushan, on the night of the 15th, 35 rice boats were exported, all loaded with large-sized rice boats, averaging 100 dan per boat, totaling as many as 3,500 shi, an alarming number. At a time when there is a food shortage, a large number of rice boats are being exported, which is related to the future of the county's food supply. Therefore, citizens of the area are requesting the county government to devise ways to prevent this to maintain the food supply.

Changzhou: Construction Department Sends Personnel to Set Up Water Pumping Stations 113

There is also a need for pumps, which are not easy for the Construction Department to purchase. The Hou Sheng Ironworks in the county has more than ten pumps in stock, which they plan to purchase nearby. Various issues have been contacted with the Construction Department through long-distance telephone and are progressing. Wujin County has also been suffering from a prolonged drought and intense heat, eagerly hoping for rain. At 0:20 PM on the 16th, there was a sudden rain for twenty minutes, and again at around 4:00 PM in the evening, there was a heavy rain for thirty minutes. However, the total rainfall was less than one inch for both times. If there can be more continued heavy rainfall, there is still hope for saving the crops. There is also the issue of rice prices, which is of great importance to the people's food supply. Pinghu: Young Man in Western Suit Attempts Suicide by Drowning 120

Ningbo: Salt Police Kills Person While Suppressing Smuggling 121

In Mi Yan in Zhangcun, Yinzhou County, there was a person named Ying Along, who was over thirty years old and made his living as a farmer. Local News: 3.5 Million Yuan of Municipal Public Bonds Fully Subscribed Yesterday; Applications Exceeding 20 Million Yuan, Proportional Allocation Implemented; Supervision Committee Formed, Cai Zengji Appointed Chairman 122

The Shanghai Municipal Government issued 3.5 million yuan of municipal public bonds for the 23rd year of the Republic, underwritten by Sin Feng Bank. Subscriptions began yesterday, with numerous applicants, and the entire amount was sold out. A supervision committee has been formed and is in operation. Details are as follows:

Enthusiastic Subscription 123

After Sin Feng Bank, the managing underwriter of the public bonds, announced the subscription, many Chinese and foreign individuals requested application forms and subscribed. From 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM yesterday, subscriptions were openly conducted at the trust department of the Bank of China on Renji Road. The total amount reached over 20 million yuan, and it was immediately allocated according to the announced method. The large number of subscribers is unprecedented in the history of public bond issuance. All subscribers of these public bonds must also pay interest from June 30 to July 17. The Bank of China has decided to issue public bond certificates and refund part of the money from today based on bank receipts.

Timely Payment: 124

Sin Feng Bank's underwriting is calculated based on an issue price of 93 yuan per 100 yuan face value. It is decided that the 3,255,000 yuan that should be paid to the Shanghai Municipal Government will be paid in full within seven days from yesterday in accordance with the underwriting contract, and the National Debt Fund Management Committee is entrusted to collect donations from the Municipal Government's agencies that collect donations for automobile and other license plates to prepare for the principal and interest payments of the public bonds. The China, Communications, and Central Banks are the representatives of the National Debt Fund Management Committee.

Establishment of Supervisory Committee 125

The task of the supervisory committee is to supervise whether the use of public bonds issued by the municipal government meets the stipulated purpose. The City Suffers Severe Heat for Twenty-Three Days, Light Rain Finally Arrives Yesterday Afternoon; Showers in the Afternoon and Evening; Long-Awaited Land Still Not Fully Soaked 126

The city had rain once on June 23, but after June 25, it was severely hot for days on end. There was some thunder in the afternoons of July 12 and 13, but until the day before yesterday, not a drop of rain had fallen, causing farmland in various villages to crack, seedlings to wither, and the autumn harvest to seem hopeless. The municipal government established a drought prevention committee, and various charitable organizations also set up altars to pray for rain, but despite the eager hope for rain, there was still no sign of it. It was not until noon yesterday that the sky began to cloud over, and at around 12:40 PM, it began to rain, but it only lasted for about an hour, so the long-awaited land was not fully soaked. However, the heat has noticeably decreased, and the epidemic may also hopefully subside slightly. According to an investigation of the rainfall and time yesterday, it varied in different places, with the central district of the concession being the largest. It started at 12:40 PM, only seeing a light drizzle, and then suddenly changed to a shower at 12:50 PM, which was quite rapid, but only lasted for more than ten minutes and then turned to a drizzle, intermittent, until it cleared completely at 2:00 PM, and the scorching sun spread across the land again, and the heat returned. The city and suburban districts were next, starting to rain at 12:45 PM and stopping after about forty minutes. The Zhabei area had rain at around 1:15 PM and stopped, and then continued at 1:45 PM, clearing up at 2:30 PM. Other areas such as Pudong, Lujiazui in the South City, and Xujiahui, Dianru, and Longhua had very little rainfall, only lasting for five or six minutes. Caojiadu and Beixinjing had no rain at all. After entering the evening, there was another shower at around 10:25 PM, similar to the daytime, but it only lasted for more than ten minutes and did not result in soaking rain. Therefore, the climate turned muggy, and the hospitals in the city saw a slight decrease in patients due to the temporary cooling after the rain.

The Dredging Bureau Dispatches Large Pumps to Irrigate Pudong Farmland; Can Draw 3,500 Tons of Water per Hour; Song ZiLiang Consults City Government to Quickly Send Workers to Build Dams 127

Since the beginning of summer, the city has experienced a shortage of rainfall and the weather has been severely dry, which has not occurred in decades. The crops in the fields have withered. If we do not promptly seek relief, there will be no hope for an autumn harvest and people's food security will be at risk. It is understood that Song Ziliang, Director of the Dredging Bureau, has recognized this and has now decided to dispatch several engineers to transport two special pumps from the bureau to the Pudong area to draw water for urgent relief. It is estimated that each pump can draw 3,500 tons of water per hour, averaging 84,000 tons per day, which is a groundbreaking water pumping machine for Shanghai. It is also understood that Mr. Song specifically petitioned the Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday to quickly dispatch workers to build dams, so that they can irrigate the farmland as soon as possible to comfort the farmers' hopes.

Fire Brigades in Various Districts Continue to Dispatch Water Pumping; However, They Complain That the Belts Are Still Too Short and Insufficient for Use; The Municipal Public Security Bureau Is Actively Trying to Find a Solution 128

Due to the recent dry weather in the city, the Public Security Bureau, following the order of the municipal government, purchased water pumps and distributed them to various rural districts for use. Since there was no time to rush the process, in order to urgently relieve rural farmlands, the bureau specifically instructed Dong Jiaoyuan, a fire prevention section member of the Second Section, to urge the city's nine fire brigades to depart for the various rural districts to be responsible for pumping water the day before yesterday. It is understood that when the fire brigades went to various rural districts to pump water and irrigate crops the day before yesterday, the general farmers, upon seeing them, were all beaming with joy, and provided food and water to the firefighters. However, the areas in the various districts were vast, and the belts were deemed insufficient for use. Therefore, yesterday morning, several representatives from the various Zhabei fire brigade branches went to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to petition for permission to purchase tens of thousands of feet of additional belts. The bureau has indicated that it is currently actively planning funding and will find a way to purchase them in the shortest amount of time. It is reported that the amount is in the tens of thousands of yuan, and the firefighters will continue to depart for the various rural districts to pump water today.

Gu Xinyi Discusses Reasons for Ordering Foreign Rice; Represents the Opinions of the Rice Industry 129

The Central News Agency reported that, recently, it was reported that the city's rice merchants, in view of the severe drought and disaster, plan to order 500,000 shi of foreign rice from foreign merchants to help stabilize rice prices. Mr. Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the City's Bean and Rice Industry Association, issued the following statement to reporters from the Central News Agency:

This Year's Rise Is Rare 130

According to Mr. Gu, in recent years, rice prices have plummeted, causing panic in the rural economy. However, recently, due to severe drought, the general public is deeply concerned that a major disaster will occur, so rice prices have risen. Although this happens every year at this time when the new harvest is not yet available, the rapid rise in prices this year is rare, which is unfavorable for the people's food supply, and the impact on farmers is also not insignificant. Therefore, the city's rice merchants have a proposal to purchase foreign rice to stabilize rice prices.

Yangon Rice Is Cheaper 131

The rice merchants are now planning to order 500,000 shi of foreign rice from Yangon. China imports a large amount of foreign rice every year, mostly from Saigon. However, this year, India also suffered a disaster, so Saigon rice is being shipped to India for sale. However, Yangon should have surplus rice for export, and the price is cheaper. At current market prices, it is roughly around 10 yuan, which is about 2-3 yuan cheaper than the current price of rice in our country. Therefore, if this foreign rice is imported, rice prices can definitely be stabilized.

Extensive Drought Area 132

Our reporter has learned that external sources do not believe China's existing rice reserves necessitate imports of foreign rice. Concerns have been raised that importing foreign rice could depress domestic rice prices, repeating past mistakes. When questioned, Mr. Gu stated that the drought-stricken area this year is very large, and even with thunderstorms during this hot season, it will be difficult to remedy. In past years with good harvests, large quantities of foreign rice were still imported, which undoubtedly greatly impacted domestic rice prices. However, rice merchants in this city currently plan to order no more than 500,000 shih of foreign rice, and they can reduce the quantity if it is deemed excessive. Therefore, it is not expected to have any significant impact on the domestic rice market.

Rice Industry Submits Request to the Executive Yuan for Approval 133

Mr. Gu further stated that although rice merchants in this city have this plan, it still needs to be submitted to the central government for approval. The purpose of ordering foreign rice is solely to alleviate concerns about the future rice market. If a drought and famine unfortunately occur this year, not only will there be panic regarding the food supply in cities, but also rice riots in rural areas. Therefore, for the sake of the overall food supply and local security, it seems necessary to plan and take preventative measures as soon as possible. The Rice Industry Association of this city stated in its submission to the Executive Yuan that the purchase of foreign rice would be limited to 500,000 shih, with no private imports allowed. Furthermore, the sales and pricing will be comprehensively planned. The government will likely submit this matter to relevant departments for study, and then to the Civil Food Control Design Committee for planning. If the government deems this matter feasible, the rice industry in this city will immediately raise funds to purchase the rice to meet urgent needs.

Large Quantities of Russian Rice to Arrive in Shanghai, Rice Prices Expected to Fall 134

The World News Agency reports that this year, various regions of our country have suffered severe droughts since the beginning of summer. The fields have turned into cracked earth, and the crops have withered and turned yellow, creating a desolate scene. As a result, rice prices in this city have soared, rising to over four yuan in just two or three weeks. Rice merchants have submitted a request to the government to waive import taxes and purchase large quantities of foreign rice in preparation for famine. Yesterday, news from the transportation industry revealed that after the success of the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan, the active promotion of production has led to a surplus of agricultural and industrial products. Upon hearing of the sudden rise in rice prices in our country, they believed it was an opportunity not to be missed and are shipping large quantities of surplus Russian rice to China with the intention of dumping it. It is reported that the quantity is as high as hundreds of thousands of dan, and it has already set sail from Vladivostok to Shanghai. It is expected to arrive within a week. Rice merchants in this city have received this news, and rice prices are already showing a downward trend.

American Businessman Promotes Chinese Goods, Collects Over 150 Varieties, Plans to Ship to Europe and America for Promotion 135

The Central News Agency reports that Mr. Sparck, an American businessman who has been engaged in the import business in China for a long time, believes that Chinese domestic goods are improving rapidly and are popular with foreigners. Therefore, he has raised funds to organize a company dedicated to promoting Chinese domestic goods. He has already collected over 150 varieties of high-quality Chinese domestic goods and is holding an exhibition at his company on the second floor of the Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation building, which has been praised by foreigners. Mr. Sparck and others believe that the demand for Chinese domestic goods is very high in Southeast Asia and other regions. Therefore, they have packed the goods and are scheduled to ship them to various ports in Southeast Asia this Friday on the President Cleveland of the Dollar Steamship Lines. From there, they will be distributed to India and other European and American countries for promotion.

Bureau of Foreign Trade Introduces British and American Businesses to Purchase Chinese Products, London Purchases Novelties, America Needs Soybean Flour 136

According to the Guidance Department of the International Trade Bureau, China's foreign trade is currently indirect, handled by foreign firms, which is inconvenient for both Chinese and foreign importers and exporters. Therefore, the bureau is vigorously promoting direct trade, which has gained the trust of foreign businesses. They often write to the bureau requesting the introduction of Chinese products for sale overseas. In order to develop foreign trade, the bureau immediately informs domestic goods manufacturers to contact them for promotion. In this time of market depression, it is urgent to open up overseas markets to help Chinese producers. The following is a description of the Chinese products that European and American importers are requesting to be introduced: Attwater & Sons, a London company, plans to manage various novelties and fancy goods manufactured in China. Wallis Plaster Company needs sorghum stalks for certain manufacturing purposes. Export firms interested in trading with this company are requested to send quotations. An American glue company needs soybean flour. Siam Silmore Company needs electrical materials such as lampshades, light bulbs, fans, heaters, bakelite switches, and wall sockets. Trading firms interested in being entrusted with the management can contact the company directly. The address of the International Trade Bureau is on the fourth floor of the Jianghai Customs House.
