Preparing to Dredge the Shentan Shoal, Dredging Vessels Will Arrive Soon, Sounding Work to Begin First 141

The Central News Agency reports that the issue of dredging the Shentan Shoal at the mouth of the Yangtze River to facilitate navigation is being carried out by the Dredging Bureau in conjunction with the Hydrographic Survey Bureau. The Dredging Bureau has purchased dredging vessels from foreign companies, which will arrive in Shanghai soon. Therefore, it has consulted the Hydrographic Survey Bureau to conduct a sounding of the Shentan Shoal beforehand. The details are as follows:

Current Situation of the Shentan Shoal 142

The Shentan Shoal is located at the mouth of the Yangtze River, very close to the mouth of the Huangpu River. It is a necessary passage for ships entering and leaving. Because the mouth of the Yangtze River is located downstream, the water flow is relatively slow. Therefore, the water from the upstream carries sand downstream, which stagnates and accumulates here, increasing day by day. The Shentan Shoal is approximately 26 feet below the water surface. After being hit by wind and waves, the depth is only about 20 feet. As a result, ships with deeper drafts have great difficulty entering and leaving. The Dredging Bureau and the Hydrographic Survey Bureau, in view of this, have decided to dredge it to facilitate navigation.

Dredging Vessels Will Arrive Soon 143

After the dredging plan was decided, it was found that the work was difficult due to the Shentan Shoal being close to the sea and a vast expanse of water. In addition, there was a lack of dredging equipment. Therefore, two new-style dredging vessels were ordered from foreign companies two years ago, each worth approximately 2.5 million yuan. The vessels are custom-made, so it took a long time. It is reported that one of the vessels has been completed and will arrive in Shanghai soon. The Dredging Bureau will begin dredging as soon as the vessels arrive in Shanghai. Therefore, it is necessary to conduct a sounding of the Shentan Shoal beforehand to facilitate the work.

Sounding Work Underway 144

Regarding the sounding of the Shentan Shoal, the Dredging Bureau has recently consulted the Hydrographic Survey Bureau to handle it. Therefore, the Hydrographic Survey Bureau has been sending technicians on survey ships to the Shentan Shoal to place water gauges and conduct soundings. However, due to the strong winds and waves outside the Song Estuary in recent days, it is not easy to place the water gauges. Therefore, it has been decided to wait until the winds and waves subside slightly before proceeding. It is expected that after two sounding operations, a report will be submitted to the Dredging Bureau for dredging.

New Submarine Cable Laid at the Mouth of the Yangtze River, Shanghai Port, Navigators Take Note 145

The Hydrographic Survey Bureau has issued a notice regarding the laying of a new submarine cable in the new waterway of Gaoqiao Sand at the mouth of the Yangtze River, Shanghai Port, to alert navigators. The location of the new submarine cable is in the lower section of Shanghai Port, 700 feet south of the Customs Explosives Warehouse Wharf on the right bank of Huangpu River, from 272 degrees true north to the left bank of the river, approximately 121 degrees 33 minutes east longitude and 31 degrees 19 minutes north latitude.

Representatives of Tobacco and Liquor Industries Petition the Chamber of Commerce Yesterday, Requesting License Tax to Be Collected According to Previous Rates, Willing to Suspend Business If Goals Are Not Met 146

Chen Liangyu, Xu Yunxiang, Shen Weiting, Zhang Songji, representatives of the Shanghai Tobacco Exchange Association; Zhu Ligong, representatives of the Restaurant Association; Lan Qinghe, representatives of the Sauce and Liquor Association; Li Baogen, representatives of the Western Tobacco Association; Yang Qiaosheng, Liao Zhongwen, and over 50 other representatives of the Fenjiu Association, petitioned the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM due to concerns that the burden would increase after the license tax was transferred to the city government. They were received by Chairman Yu Zuoting and Secretary Yan Esheng. The representatives submitted a petition stating: "Regarding the petition, the associations were previously concerned that the collecting authorities would not be able to fully understand the special circumstances of Shanghai after the license tax was transferred to the city government, and that members would not be able to bear the burden if they were bound by departmental regulations. Therefore, the associations sent a letter to your chamber requesting protection, and it was reported to the municipal government, which sympathized with the difficulties of businesses. The associations also dispatched representatives to the Municipal Bureau of Finance to explain the special circumstances of Shanghai and the historical evolution, requesting Section Chief Wang to report to the Director, taking into consideration the situation of businesses, and to follow the usual practice of exchanging old licenses for new licenses. However, to this day, there has been no reply, and the number of old licenses for each store has been doubled, causing panic among the people. They have come to the association one after another, saying that each store is a small business and cannot bear such a heavy burden. Moreover, recently, housing prices have increased and foreign prices have soared. Even if taxes are paid as before, it is difficult to support. If the situation is further aggravated, they will inevitably close down one after another. Reluctantly, they have jointly elected representatives and submitted a petition, requesting your chamber to report to the mayor, taking into consideration the difficulties of businesses, and to allow the exchange of old licenses for new licenses as before. At the same time, they request the Municipal Bureau of Finance to temporarily ease the increase in tax rates to avoid disputes and ensure business operations. They will be extremely grateful." The petitioning representatives also explained the difficult business conditions, stating that they would be willing to suspend business if their concerns were not addressed. Chairman Yu Zuoting of the Chamber of Commerce comforted them, urging them to continue operating as usual and assuring them that the Chamber would submit the petition to the municipal government, urging them to sympathize with the difficulties of businesses and collect taxes as before. The representatives were satisfied and left.

Taxpayers Association Sends Letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council Based on the Original Letter from the Jianghuai Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai 150

The Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Shanghai International Settlement sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "Sir, we have received a letter from the Jianghuai Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai, stating that Yang Hailin, a fellow-provincial from Funing, reported that he lives at No. 5, Fulan Lane, Zha Pu Road, Hongkou, and is currently a recruiter for the Fourth Group of the Seventh Division of the Military Affairs Commission. He received a message asking him to return to Shanghai for leave and learned that on the 27th of the previous month, at 9:00 PM, his wife was enjoying the cool air at the entrance of the alley when she suddenly saw a rickshaw puller pulling a Japanese sailor. The sailor stopped in front of the Donghe Pavilion on this road without paying the rickshaw fare, and instead beat the rickshaw puller. Yang's wife told the rickshaw puller to escape quickly to avoid being injured. The sailor became angry at Yang's wife and accused her of assault, causing her to bleed and be seriously injured. Yang's wife cried for help. The sailor, seeing that he had caused trouble, fled north. Two Chinese and Western constables happened to pass by. Yang's wife complained to them, but three plainclothes Japanese men prevented her from speaking and dragged her south. The two constables, seeing this injustice, wanted to take the sailor and Yang's wife to the police station to resolve the matter, but the three Japanese men prevented them from doing so and shouted to beat them. The Western constable blew his whistle for help. The Japanese sailor forcibly took the Western constable and Yang's wife to the Japanese military headquarters. The Japanese took the Western constable's defensive handgun. Yang's wife escaped and reported the situation to the police station. The police station sent officers to the Japanese military headquarters to negotiate, but they were met by a large number of Japanese soldiers armed with guns. The police station sent Yang's wife to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Yang's wife was afraid of being retaliated against by the Japanese and dared not be hospitalized. She also had financial difficulties and could not afford medical treatment. Now Yang's wife is in pain all over her body, unable to sit or lie down, and in extreme danger. She requests negotiations." The association believes that Yang Hailin's wife was brutally beaten by the Japanese for speaking up to help a rickshaw puller, and the Western constable was also arrested and humiliated. The association believes that the residents of the settlement have no protection of their personal freedom and residential safety, which is extremely dangerous. The association requests the Council to investigate the situation and negotiate with the Shanghai Municipal Council to punish the perpetrators and compensate for medical expenses. The association believes that the safety of the residents of the International Settlement should be protected by the Council's police officers, which is an unavoidable responsibility under the current circumstances. Otherwise, there is no point in the residents paying for municipal expenses. Therefore, the association requests the Council to investigate the association's letter and take action as soon as possible.

Supplementary Agreement to the Joint Transportation Contract Between the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and the Zhenjiang-Danyang-Jintan-Liyang Long-Distance Bus Company 151

The Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and the Zhenjiang-Danyang-Jintan-Liyang Long-Distance Bus Company, which operates between Zhenjiang and Jintan, have been providing joint transportation for passengers, luggage, and parcels since March 1 of this year. The company changed its regulations on free luggage allowance and excess baggage charges on April 15, and added round-trip tickets between the railway's connecting stations. It also revised bus fares on May 25 and stipulated parcel rates on June 25. The railway's transportation department has signed a supplementary agreement to the joint transportation contract with the company, with three clauses to supplement it. The full text is as follows: The company's Jintan station and the railway's connecting stations will issue round-trip sightseeing tickets. The company will change its regulations on free luggage allowance and excess baggage charges. The company will revise one-way and round-trip sightseeing ticket prices and stipulate parcel rates. After consultation and supplementation, three additional clauses have been drafted for both parties to comply with: (1) Starting from May 25, 1934, the one-way ticket price from the company's Jintan station to Danyang station will be changed to 80 cents. See the attached table for joint ticket prices. (2) Starting from April 15, 1934, the company's Jintan station will issue special express and regular passenger round-trip sightseeing tickets to the railway's Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Changzhou, Wuxi, Suzhou, and Shanghai North stations. The ticket price calculation is as follows: The price from the company's Jintan station to the railway's Miaoyang station will be 1.80 yuan for all train classes and grades round-trip, and will be changed to 1.50 yuan from May 25, 1934. The prices from Danyang to the railway's connecting stations will be charged according to the railway's original round-trip fares. The validity period is two days to reach the destination from the date of departure, and the return trip is valid for ten days. The day of ticket issuance is counted as one day. All ticket prices are listed in the attached table. (3) Starting from April 15, 1934, the company's free luggage allowance for joint transportation will be changed from 15 kilograms to 30 kilograms. The excess baggage charge will be changed from 10 cents per 10 kilograms to 5 cents per 10 kilograms or less. Starting from June 25, 1934, the parcel rate will be 10 cents per 10 kilograms or less. The company may refuse to transport any luggage or parcels that weigh more than 130 kilograms or are excessively bulky. Clause A of Article 6 of the contract should be cancelled.

Five Provinces Transportation Exhibition to Display Young People's Literary and Art Works - Specifically Soliciting Creations of Unknown Young Writers and Painters in the Country - Scheduled for Public Exhibition at the YMCA on the 19th and 20th 162

To broadly solicit and promote cultural exchange, Chairman Chiang of Nanchang specifically instructed the Southeast Five Provinces Joint Highway Bureau to organize the Southeast Five Provinces Transportation Exhibition, to widely collect works from young people and promote Southeast culture. Following the order, Zeng Yangfu, Director of the Five Provinces Highway Bureau and concurrently Director of the Zhejiang Construction Department, immediately began preparations. This reporter from the *Shen Shi* newspaper met yesterday with Mr. Wang Yingbin, Secretary of the Department, who stated that after receiving the order, Director Zeng first organized a Solicitation of Young People's Literary and Art Works Committee to be responsible for handling the solicitation. After the committee was established in the spring of this year, it stipulated the solicitation methods: (1) Eligibility: Based on the literary and artistic creations of unknown young people in the country; (2) Solicitation materials: Divided into four categories: (A) Paintings, such as landscapes, etc.; (B) Western paintings, such as oil paintings, watercolors, etc.; (C) Literature, such as travel notes, articles, etc.; (D) Poetry; (3) All solicited literary and artistic works that pass the review of the Solicitation Committee will be issued a free travel pass, allowing them to freely travel throughout the five southeastern provinces to investigate cultural relics and scenery for writing various literary and artistic works to be displayed at the Transportation Exhibition; (4) Award method: All solicited works, after collection, will be evaluated by experts hired by the Exhibition. The first to fourth place winners in each of the above four categories will be given bonuses, with 300 yuan for first place, 200 yuan for second place, 100 yuan for third place, and 50 yuan for fourth place, as encouragement. The committee has decided to hold an exhibition on October 19th and 20th. More than 80 young writers who passed the preliminary review have already completed long-term investigations and travel, and have successively submitted more than 80 works. Currently, to arouse the interest of people from all walks of life in modern literary and artistic transportation, the collected works will be publicly exhibited at the YMCA in the Bāxiānqiáo area of this city on the 19th and 20th of this month before the general review by the conference. No admission tickets will be charged, and anyone can visit. Among the works are dozens of Chinese and Western paintings, all of which are outstanding works, and dozens of literary poems, representing the culmination of modern young people's creations, which are especially precious and valuable compared to any painting and calligraphy exhibition. It is thought that those who care about modern literary and artistic transportation will certainly want to see them first.

Boy Drowns While Swimming 164

Liu Jinxing, a native of Baoding, residing at No. 10 Laide Lane, Yangshupu Road, works as a laborer. He has a son named Lin Gen, who is just eleven years old. Recently, due to the hot weather, at around 2:00 PM the day before, he invited five or six neighborhood children to go swimming in the Héngdān Road river. Yesterday morning, Tang Peixian, a prosecutor appointed by the First Special District Local Court, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan, secretary Wang Zuyi, etc., arrived at the office. Upon examining the body, they stated, "The deceased, Liu Lin Gen, male, was confirmed to have drowned. Fire at Paint Shop Caused by Discarded Cigarette Butt - Apprentice Smoker Sentenced to Three Months Imprisonment 166

The Rénchāng Paint Shop, located at No. 295 Gōngpíng Road, Xīhuá Road, Gōng'an Lane, caught fire at 12:10 AM the night before, causing extensive damage and spreading to neighboring houses at No. 293 and No. 297. Five people, including Wèi Gēn Bǎo, were burned. After the incident, Chinese detective Shen Binkui and Yà Yǒnglè from the local police station went to investigate and learned that the fire was caused by Pǔ Shuǐjīn, a Suzhou apprentice hired by the shop owner, Yè Shēngxiáng, who discarded a cigarette butt near the paint materials before going to bed. The detectives believed that Pǔ was at fault and arrested him. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Fifth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Lawyer Jiang Baolian from the police station explained the case and prosecuted him under Article 187, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. Under questioning by Judge Huang Risheng, the defendant confessed that he had smoked a cigarette before going to bed, but did not know if it caused the fire. Mr. Huang then sentenced Pǔ to three months of street imprisonment as a warning.

Fire on Tiantong'an Road, Zhabei, Yesterday Morning - Five Families in Xingyu Lane Suffer 167

A fire suddenly broke out at around 2:40 AM yesterday morning at the home of a certain family at No. 17 Xingyu Lane, Tiantong'an Road, Zhabei. At that time, all the residents were already asleep, so they did not notice the fire immediately. By the time neighbors caught sight of it and shouted for help, it had already broken through the roof, and the flames were soaring into the sky, making it impossible to approach. In addition, the weather was dry and arid, making the fire easy to spread. Therefore, it soon spread to the five neighboring houses at No. 16, No. 15, No. 14, No. 13, and No. 12. For a time, the raging flames soared, and the fire illuminated the sky. The residents were all awakened from their dreams, helping the elderly and carrying the young, fleeing for their lives in a chaotic and disorderly manner. The nearby roadside was blocked by boxes and luggage from the lane residents, and the shouts and cries were extremely noisy. Fortunately, the fire brigades in each section had received the alarm at this time and drove to the scene to provide assistance. At the same time, the Fifth District Office also dispatched a large number of long-term police officers to suppress the situation, and order was gradually restored. However, because the fire was aided by the wind, it was not easy to extinguish. The firefighters tried their best to prevent it from spreading, and bravely sprayed water until around 5:00 AM at dawn, when it was completely extinguished. As a result, in addition to half of the house at No. 12 being destroyed, the rest were turned to ashes, resulting in heavy losses. The arsonist at No. 17, where the fire started, fled after the fire broke out, so he was not arrested. At the same time, the cause of the fire is also unknown. However, according to a group of neighbors, it is feared that it was caused by catching insects in the mosquito net, leaving fire on the net. The police station is currently investigating and pursuing the arsonist, and will bring him to justice for interrogation.

Fire on Fangxie Road Last Night - Guangfeng Dyeing and Weaving Factory Destroys Four Houses 168

At 7:35 PM last night, a fire suddenly broke out at Guangfeng Dyeing and Weaving Factory, located at No. 2, Lane 91, Anlan Road, Fangxie Road, Nanshi, and immediately spread. The Second District General Office reported to the fire brigade, who rushed to the scene to put out the fire. It took about half an hour of spraying water before it was extinguished. In this incident, four factory buildings were destroyed, and the losses are pending investigation. The authorities are investigating the cause of the fire.

Marital Dispute Between Englishman and Russian Woman 169

An Englishman, Ah Baike (transliteration), 44 years old, employed by an oil company, resides in Room 23, Bīài sī Apartment, Fēnglù Road. On May 10th of this year, he met a Russian girl, Sha Gulov (transliteration), 16 years old (residing at No. 19307 Fèidé Road) at a friend's place. They exchanged affections and felt as if they had met too late. They lived together like a couple. Unexpectedly, before long, a storm arose in their love affair. Ah Baike immediately retained lawyer Huang Qiying to file a petition with the Second Special Court Mediation Tribunal, requesting to terminate the cohabitation relationship. The petition stated that when they met, they were in agreement with each other, and on May 20th, they went to a Russian church to hold a wedding ceremony. However, because the petitioner is of British nationality, it cannot be considered legal, and the opposing party also expressed understanding of this point. They were to complete the marriage ceremony at the British Consulate to make it legal. Subsequently, on June 8th, a marriage permit was obtained from the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau for the purpose of getting married at the British Consulate. Unexpectedly, the attitude of the opposing party suddenly changed, refusing to marry the petitioner and demanding to be separated from him. Her intentions are unpredictable, and they cannot continue to cohabit or cooperate as a family. The court approved the petition and summoned them yesterday morning. Now, in order to avoid his responsibility, the petitioner first came to the court to apply for mediation. Now the opposing party is preparing to file a complaint against the petitioner at the British Consulate. Judge Li Liang ruled that the mediation in this case was unsuccessful and instructed the petitioner to file a separate lawsuit.

Hu Zhou Shi, 27 years old, the wife of Hu Yusheng, a Ningbo native residing at No. 68 Danfeng Road, Xinkaihe, Nanshi, is by nature fierce. In late April of this year, after having a quarrel with her husband, she left in a fit of anger. She took the opportunity to lure her and tricked Hu Zhou Shi into her home at No. 247, Lan Wei'ai Road, in the French Concession. Unexpectedly, she lost consciousness in an instant and fell asleep on the bed. Although she regained consciousness slightly the next day, her mind was still dizzy and she wanted to sleep. She slept for ten days in a row. During this period, Jiang Qiaoshi, along with Yang Jucai, Yang Gouda, Liu Guifang, and others, tried to sell Hu Zhou Shi for a price. Shen Baofa, a Pudong native who opened a leather suitcase shop at No. 707 Labosheng Road in West Shanghai, had a surplus of hundreds of yuan from his business during the Jing'an Temple incense festival on April 8th and was eager to marry a concubine. Shen and Yang Jucai, and others, were familiar with each other, so Yang and others acted as matchmakers and sold Hu Zhou Shi to Shen as a concubine, agreeing on a price of 80 yuan and a matchmaking fee of 20 yuan. At the beginning of last month, Jiang Qiaoshi, Yang Jucai, and others sent Hu Zhou Shi to Shen's place and signed an agreement. Shen paid the price and matchmaking fee in full and gave 3 yuan for the car fare. At that time, after Hu Zhou Shi entered the door, she was greatly favored by Shen, and they were very affectionate. However, good things do not last long, and her nature was difficult to change. Before a month had passed, she argued with Shen again. Later, she learned that she was a concubine and became furious. At the beginning of this month, she ran away from Shen behind his back and returned to her husband, Hu Yusheng. She reported the details of being deceived and sold one by one. Upon learning this, Hu was extremely angry. The afternoon before, he accompanied her to Shen's place to negotiate. The two sides were arguing and about to resort to violence when the West District Detective Team learned of it and arrested everyone at the Sixth District and went to the French Concession to arrest Jiang Qiaoshi, Qiao Daoren, Yang Jucai, Yang Gouda, and Liu Guifang. After interrogating them separately, Xing, a district official, determined that the case involved enticing a married woman and conspiring to sell her. He immediately prepared a document to send to the bureau for interrogation.

Shanghai Industrial Trust Corporation Hosts Journalists to Visit Gaoqiao Seaside - Eighty-Plus Reporters from Chinese and Foreign Newspapers Attend - Departed at 2 PM, Returned to the Bund at Approximately 7 PM 173

The Shanghai Industrial Trust Corporation and the Municipal Ferry Management Office hosted reporters from various Chinese and foreign newspapers in the city at Gaoqiao Seaside yesterday (the 17th) at 3 PM. Guests and hosts enjoyed themselves thoroughly, and each returned at dusk. Details are recorded as follows:

Equipment on the Ferry 174

Around 1 PM yesterday, reporters from Chinese and Western newspapers successively arrived at the bronze statue pier on the Bund, Nanjing Road. By 2 PM, all guests had assembled, totaling more than eighty people. They were hosted by Tan Boying, the manager of the corporation, and Chen Kecheng from the municipal government, and set sail on time. The ferry used yesterday was the No. 5 ferry, the newest type of ferryboat in the office, specially opened for the reporters. All the equipment was very clean, and the first and second class cabins were especially spacious and comfortable, with very good ventilation. The equipment in the special class was extremely magnificent, but there were not many seats. This type of ferryboat is specially designed for the general public, and there are relatively few special class passengers. However, the front and rear decks were very wide, filled with canvas chairs, and could accommodate hundreds of people. The floor was also very smooth and could be used for dancing. The ferry was equipped with a wireless radio, and elegant music played softly while the ferry was sailing. The sparkling waves and shadows of the clouds in the Huangpu River, and the clear and beautiful scenery, made the guests extremely happy. After an hour's journey, they arrived at Gaoqiao.

Seaside Tour 175

After arriving at Gaoqiao, they changed to a special car prepared by the corporation and drove for about fifteen minutes to the seaside. First, they took a short break at the Seaside Hotel and were served refreshments. Then, they went to the seaside one after another for sightseeing. The seaside had calm waters and bright sand, stretching as far as the eye could see. Reporters who were good at swimming changed their clothes and went to the sea one after another to try their skills, chasing the waves and floating. They were very interested. After everyone had been sightseeing at the seaside for a long time, they took a special car back to Gaoqiao Pier and boarded the special ferry back to Shanghai. The speech of Tan Boying, the manager of the corporation, to the reporters in the ferry is recorded below.

Tan's Speech 176

Tan Boying, the manager of the corporation, said, "Today, I am very honored to have the presence of reporters from Chinese and Western newspapers. I dare to offer a few words, and I hope you will give me your wise guidance. The municipal government's establishment of the municipal ferry was originally intended to facilitate the water transportation of the general public, not specifically for sightseeing purposes. Therefore, the equipment must be as complete as possible, and the ticket price must be as low as possible. We are working hard to improve every day. Fortunately, the results have been slightly noticeable in these few years. Gentlemen and ladies from all walks of life do not find the equipment on the ferry simple, and often take the ferry for excursions during their leisure time. The corporation adapts to the needs of society and operates evening cooling shifts in the summer. However, most of the passengers on the ferry are still travelers, and fewer are tourists. The corporation's greatest effort is still to adhere to the municipal government's intention and pay attention to the welfare of the general public. This is one aspect. The ferry equipment must not be too simple to ensure the safety of passengers. However, the prices of materials have soared recently, such as fuel and labor, which have increased day by day, and the ticket price cannot be increased to increase the burden on the public. According to the income of ordinary passengers, it is almost impossible to maintain. The corporation is determined to attract tourists to seek contributions. Fortunately, the municipal government is guiding from above, and the employees are working hard below. In these few years, although we have felt extremely difficult, we still have a small surplus, which is comforting to all sectors of society. Since the municipal ferry was ordered to be transferred to the Industrial Trust Corporation for management last autumn, it has been nearly October, and all matters have progressed rapidly. The number of passengers has also increased sharply compared to the past. There are facts to prove this. This is the second aspect. Recently, the citizens of this city have been quite aware of the benefits of suburban travel for physical and mental health. Therefore, on good days in spring and autumn, many ladies and gentlemen take ferries for excursions. Initially, Westerners accounted for the majority, about eight or nine out of ten. Now, our Chinese people also know the joy of suburban travel, and many bring their families, including the elderly, the weak, women, and children, who are also very fond of sea bathing or sunbathing on the beach. This shows that the general public has a deep understanding of the new life and is putting it into practice. This is the third aspect. What I have said above is just a humble opinion. You are leaders in the world of opinion, and I hope that you will provide guidance and correction at any time to promote the realization of the great Shanghai water transportation plan. I cannot be more grateful. Today's hospitality is simple and slow, and I am very ashamed."

Interrogation of Longhua Temple Property Infringement Case Held Again Yesterday - More Witnesses Need to Be Summoned 177

Xingkong, the abbot of Longhua Temple, filed a lawsuit in the local court against the former abbot, Yuanzhao, and Hu Suji for conspiring to establish a contract to infringe on temple property, demanding confirmation that the mortgage management and rent collection contract signed by Yuanzhao and others was invalid. The trial has been held repeatedly without a conclusion. Yesterday, Judge Wang Run specially opened the First Court to continue the trial. On the plaintiff's side, lawyers Pan Zhensheng and Yuan Xilian attended; on the defendant's side, lawyers Sha Xunyi and Chen Wenzhao attended; lawyer Yao Wenshou, representative of the participant, and the plaintiff and defendant and witnesses, etc. According to Xingkong's confession, he is 72 years old and from Emei County, Sichuan. (Question) When did you come to the temple? (Answer) November of last year. (Question) What are you suing Yuanzhao and others for? (Answer) As the abbot of Longhua Temple, I have the responsibility to protect the temple property and to organize it one by one. Because I learned that Hu Suji was hired by Yuanzhao, and they conspired to embezzle the temple property, I filed this lawsuit. At this point in the confession, the official letter of the Shanghai Buddhist Association's appointment as abbot and a diary were presented to the court for inspection. The judge read them and returned them to the court. (Question) Why did you not receive the Wànnián register from Zhao Lingshao, a member of the Buddhist Association? (Answer) If I were to receive it from the Buddhist Association, I would have to use legal procedures, so I have not yet received it. (Question) How many monks who were colleagues with Yuanzhao when he was the abbot are still in the temple? (Answer) Yuanzhao's disciples, Fang Shen and Fang Hua, are still in the temple. The judge then questioned Yuanzhao, Hu Suji, and the witnesses, and ordered Yuanzhao and Hu Suji to submit additional evidence, and scheduled another hearing to summon Fang Shen, Fang Hua, and others for a joint interrogation, in order to verify the facts. After the announcement, the court adjourned.

Quarrel Over a Slice of Watermelon Leads to Husband Stabbing Wife - Knife Pierces Lung - Injuries Are Very Serious 178

Zhou Maoda, a local resident residing in a bungalow without a number on Hejian Road, is 40 years old. Recently, he has been unemployed and living off his savings at home, and his finances are extremely tight. His wife, Lou, often quarrels with him. At 10:15 AM the day before, his eleven-year-old daughter, Shi Bao, picked up a discarded slice of watermelon in front of the door and asked her father to cut off the dirt and eat it. Zhou Maoda used a fruit knife to scrape it, and Lou caught sight of it and scolded him loudly, saying, "You have no money to buy watermelon, so you pick up what other people throw away to eat!" Zhou became enraged out of shame and stabbed Lou once under her right breast with the knife. Lou was injured and fell to the ground, crying out in pain. A neighbor woman flew to report it to the No. 15 Indian policeman on duty nearby, who arrested him and took him, along with the murder weapon, to the Yangshupu Police Station. Zhou's attorney, Li Zhishan, from the 工部局 (Public Works Department), yesterday morning stated to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court that, according to the victim, the defendant did not do business and often pawned his clothes for money, while the defendant accused her of being unchaste and often returning home late at night. The victim is currently in the hospital with serious injuries, and the knife has pierced her lung, and requested an extension. He presented the injury certificate and the murder weapon for inspection. Judge Liu Yugui ordered that he be returned to custody and rescheduled the hearing for seven days later.

Concession Rickshaw Merchants Petitioned Yesterday Without Result 183

The Public Works Department believes that rickshaw owners charge rickshaw pullers 14 dimes per day for rickshaw rental, and there are head foremen and contractors who additionally demand extra money from them. This causes the average rickshaw puller, even after selling his labor all day long, to have difficulty making ends meet. Therefore, a Rickshaw Committee was established to improve the treatment of rickshaw pullers and decided to reduce the daily rental to 10 dimes starting from August 1, and to 8 dimes next year, to show relief. The rickshaw merchants in the Concession specially sent representatives Yin Zhiling and Hou Shaoan and two others to petition yesterday. It is reported that there was no result.

Public Works Department Commences Organizing the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society 184

The Management Department of the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society, initiated by the Public Works Department, was established on the 13th of this month. The Public Works Department appointed Messrs. Massey, Zhu Maocheng, and Wang Zhiren as fund committee members. Later, the committee members invited Dr. Li Denghui (President of Fudan University), Miss J. B. Perkins (Secretary of the Women's Federation Committee), Mr. R. R. Service (Secretary of the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association), Mr. Laurence Todnem (American Bible Society), Mr. Ying Shugui (Accountant of the Shanghai YMCA), and Mr. Qiu Zitong (Secretary of the Yangshupu Social Center) to form a management department. At the meeting that day, Mr. Massey presided and reported that the purpose of the society is purely for the welfare of public rickshaw pullers, and it is based on the self-reliance and mutual assistance of the rickshaw pullers. As for the society's expenses, each rickshaw puller will donate one dime per day. This amount will be collected by the rickshaw owners, who will then pay one dollar and fifty cents per rickshaw per month to the society. As for the rickshaw pullers' burden of one dime, it will not be difficult because, since August 1, the Public Works Department has stipulated that the rickshaw rental is 10 dimes per day, adding this one dime, it totals 11 dimes, which is less than the current rental of 14 dimes. Subsequently, the committee members discussed the implementation methods and decided to first select Messrs. Service, Qiu Zitong, and Zhu Maocheng to form a small committee to study the implementation procedures and submit a report at the second meeting on the 27th of this month. The committee members of the management department may be supplemented with other people in the future.

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Issues a Notice on Maintaining Outdoor Cleanliness: Violators of Cleanliness Rules Will Be Fined; Sweeping the Roads to Ensure Public Health 187

The Municipal Public Security Bureau of this city considers Shanghai to be a major port in East Asia, to which Chinese and foreigners alike pay attention. Public health and road cleanliness are extremely important. In addition to the previous notices and reminders, it distributed cleanliness guidelines yesterday morning, to be posted at each household, so that all citizens of the city can supervise each other and implement them. Those who deliberately violate them will be subject to appropriate fines. The original text is transcribed as follows: This city is a major port in East Asia, to which Chinese and foreigners alike pay attention. Public health and road cleanliness are especially important. Regulations and various penalties have long been enacted, announced, and observed. Now, the most important and most easily violated items by citizens are excerpted and listed below. It is hoped that all citizens of this city will pay attention and no longer attempt to violate them, lest they incur punishment. (1) Dumping garbage in places where there are no garbage cans, or dumping it outside the cans, will be fined. (2) Defecating or urinating in places where there are no toilets or urinals, and defecating in urinals, will be fined. (3) Dumping excrement on roads, in rivers, or in ditches will be fined. (4) Deliberately damaging road surfaces will be fined. (such as discarding leaf debris, paper, and all kinds of filth on roads.) The above excerpts are from the city's outdoor cleanliness rules. Violators will be fined from 50 cents to 5 yuan. (5) Each household has the obligation to maintain cleanliness in front of its door and within the adjacent area. If there is any damaging situation, they should immediately dissuade it. If the dissuasion is not heeded, they should be responsible for reporting the name to the competent district or nearby police for investigation and prohibition. (Article 5 of the city's outdoor cleanliness rules) (6) Discarding ice, snow, dust, gravel, filth, etc., on the road will be fined. (7) Failure to sweep the road after being urged by the public authorities will be fined. The above excerpts are from Article 42 of the Violation Penalty Rules. Violators will be fined up to 5 yuan. (8) Drying or frying any items that generate foul odors in densely populated areas, despite being prohibited, will be fined. Article 46 of the Prohibition Penalty Law. Violators will be subject to detention for up to 15 days or a fine of up to 15 yuan. (9) Mixing substances harmful to health into food and beverages to obtain illegitimate profits will be fined. Article 47 of the Prohibition Penalty Law. Violators will be subject to detention for up to 10 days or a fine of up to 10 yuan. (It is strictly forbidden to sprinkle raw water or sewage on food or to fill glass bottles with colored water as beverages. Violators will be detained and fined.) (10) Transporting feces and filth through the streets without covering them or arbitrarily stopping will be fined. (11) Urinating or defecating on roads or in public places will be fined. The above excerpts are from Article 49 of the Violation Penalty Law. Violators will be fined up to 5 yuan.

Hongqiao Sanatorium Hires Special Physicians 189

The Hongqiao Sanatorium in West Shanghai adopts the latest modern equipment and architecture. People from all countries call it the only sanatorium in the East. Reading Q&A Several Questions about Books 丨Answer to Mr. Ye Guobin丨 209

Reading Guidance:

Since joining your department, I have been eager to purchase and read the book you recommended to me, "Basic Knowledge of Social Sciences." After reading it, I have several questions, listed below, and I would appreciate your guidance.

1. In the section on social sciences in the first chapter, it states, "Social phenomena are conscious, while natural phenomena are unconscious. Social phenomena are purposeful, while natural phenomena are aimless. The labor of social phenomena and the labor of natural phenomena differ in form: the special form of labor in social phenomena is the use and creation of labor tools, which is a characteristic of humans, whereas most natural phenomena do not engage in natural labor, and even when they do, the form of their labor is different from the form of labor in social phenomena." Which natural phenomena do not engage in labor? Which ones do? I really don't understand.

2. This book only mentions social sciences and natural sciences. I don't know if philosophy and literature belong to social sciences. Can the term "philosophical science" be opposed to the terms "social science" and "natural science," or is it contained within social science?

3. The third chapter, "Social Thought," describes theories such as socialism, anarchism, and nationalism, each with its own merits. I don't know which one is more viable and beneficial to humanity. How can one distinguish between the good and bad of these social thoughts so as not to be misled by incorrect ideas?

4. Is there a difference between social thought and political thought?

The above are my questions after reading the book "Basic Knowledge of Social Sciences." However, what I am most dissatisfied with is that although this book tells me the content of social sciences, it is biased towards objective narration, leaving me unsure which social thought is correct and can be implemented for the benefit of the masses, and which social movement is most effective. Also, there are too many typos. (Rest omitted)

丨Letter from Ye Guobin

Answer 1: Natural phenomena can be divided into biological phenomena and non-biological phenomena. Biological phenomena, such as the lives of animals, require labor because animals must use their own labor to seek or capture food. Non-biological things do not need nutrients, so they do not need to labor. Although plants need nutrients, their nutrients are obtained entirely from readily available sources and do not require them to move their bodies, so there is little labor involved. Although the lives of animals depend on labor, their labor is entirely based on their own physiological structure. For example, tigers and leopards can only use claws and teeth, cattle and horses can only use horns and hooves, and elephants can only use their trunks. Therefore, it is unconscious. Humans, on the other hand, can create tools independently of their physiological structure, i.e., they can change the shape of external objects according to their own needs to suit their own needs. Therefore, it is purposeful and conscious.

Answer 2: Generally, when science is mentioned, it only refers to natural sciences and social sciences. Philosophy and literature are not included. But in reality, it cannot be divided so strictly. For example, although literature does not belong to any science in terms of creation, it must be studied as part of social science in terms of theory. Philosophy stands in a comprehensive position with regard to science. The content of philosophy is the common and general laws of social science and natural science. Therefore, philosophy can be said to be neither social science nor natural science, but it has a close relationship with both. When studying knowledge, one must not divide the various departments of knowledge too strictly and should pay attention to the interconnections of the various sciences in order not to be limited by narrow concepts.

Answer 3: Regarding the pros and cons of various doctrines, we cannot stand on a subjective position and casually answer readers, because the purpose of reading is for readers to be able to judge for themselves. As for telling readers how to distinguish between good and bad, that is possible. What are good and viable doctrines? It must be a doctrine based on scientific theory. What theory is scientific? We cannot seek the answer to this question solely in books; we must also verify it in the facts of real society. If a theory is not one-sided, exaggerated, or deceptive, but can expose the most real essence of objective facts, then everything stated by this theory must be correct, and the actions of human beings based on this theory will also be the most progressive and effective. Using these two points as standards, we can very well judge the good and bad of a doctrine. Therefore, to be able to judge accurately, one must also have some experience; one cannot immediately obtain a complete conclusion from books. Books only help us in one aspect, that is, providing some knowledge. There is absolutely no real encyclopedia in the world...

Answer 4: Political thought is a part of social thought.

Letter from the Editor: The Shen Shi Telegraphic News Agency Over the Past Decade: Past Developments 210

There are three modern tools for international competition: military affairs, economy, and propaganda. Propaganda is the vanguard in various battles around the world. Great powers devote tireless effort in organizing and managing these. The most important and successful among them are telegraphic news agencies, which are large in scale and tightly organized. Examples include Reuters in England, United Press in America, Havas in France, TASS in Russia, and Dentsu in Japan. Their capital often reaches millions, and their communication networks span the globe. Therefore, they can send a message in the morning and have it spread to all nations by evening. Their power is strong, and the results are magnificent. Since the beginning of journalism in our country, due to weak economic strength and lack of transportation, there has been no such organization. Every time there are international negotiations, we are deceived by the enemy and cannot obtain the support of correct world public opinion, leading to repeated failures in diplomacy. Furthermore, domestic newspapers, due to the lack of assistance from telegraphic news agencies, have difficulty covering events thoroughly and are slow to receive news. Important news such as political, military, and economic news is monopolized by foreign communication agencies, which distort the truth, divide national unity. Not only is it difficult to expect long-term progress, but they are also declining day by day, with no vitality. The harm they inflict on our country and nation is no less than military and economic aggression.

Ten years ago, a few people in Shanghai's newspaper industry, aware of this, contacted colleagues from the editorial departments of the Shen Bao and Shi Shi Xin Bao. During their spare time, they extracted and translated special dispatches from various sources obtained by the two newspapers and telegraphed them to several related newspapers in other cities, aiming to transmit accurate news in a swift manner, assist the development of newspapers in various regions, and correct the views of people from all walks of life. This was the beginning of the "China Times Telegraphic News Agency."

After several years of trial operation, they were deeply appreciated by newspapers in various regions, and the number of newspapers entrusting them to send telegrams increased daily. Colleagues from the two newspapers found it difficult to manage both. Therefore, in 1928, they defined the organization, expanded capital, and hired full-time staff to compile and send Chinese and English telegrams separately. The foundation of the news agency was thus laid, and the name "Shen Shi" began to be recognized by society. The news telegraphic agency operated by Chinese people has used "Shen Shi" as its beginning since then. Responding to social needs and based on the spirit of service, they gradually expanded, and business became prosperous. Chinese people gradually understood that the telegraphic news agency has a close relationship with the country and the nation. In order to develop their businesses, newspapers have paid more attention to telegraphic news agencies. The work of "Shen Shi" has been increasingly supported by all parties and has made rapid progress.

Since the January 28th Incident, the work of "Shen Shi" has suddenly become tense as it followed the Songhu Anti-Japanese War. At that time, several special military reporters from "Shen Shi" braved dangers and went to the war zone to investigate the military situation on both sides, entering and exiting the hail of bullets. Although they were often in danger, they never flinched. Internal editors worked around the clock and were often stationed at the news agency, and as soon as intelligence from the front lines arrived, they immediately compiled and sent it to newspapers in various regions. Therefore, the news obtained by "Shen Shi" was more detailed and accurate than that of foreign telegraphic agencies, and the telegrams sent were the fastest, winning great praise from all parties and regaining the hard-won honor of China's telegraphic industry. Newspapers in various regions requesting "Shen Shi" to supply telegrams have flocked in ever since. The original staff in the news agency was insufficient, so in that summer, the news agency expanded internally and hired more staff, and business has progressed even further. To date, the number of newspapers that have formally contracted with "Shen Shi" to supply telegrams, both domestically and abroad, has reached more than one hundred. Domestically, the locations include Shanghai, Suzhou, Wuxi, Zhenjiang, Nanjing, Hangzhou, Ningbo, Bengbu, Wuhu, Anqing, Jiujiang, Nanchang, Hankou, Changsha, Chongqing, Chengdu, Kunming, Guiyang, Jinan, Yantai, Tianjin, Beiping, Kaifeng, Xi'an, Fuzhou, Xiamen, Shantou, Guangzhou, and other places. Abroad, the locations include Hong Kong, Singapore, the Philippines, Java, and Honolulu. More than thirty special correspondents are stationed in various important cities. On average, more than 60,000 words are received and sent daily. Furthermore, the special telegrams received daily by the Shi Shi Xin Bao, Da Lu Bao, and Da Wan Bao are used by "Shen Shi" to the greatest extent. Therefore, "Shen Shi" is nothing less than a general collection of political, military, economic, educational, industrial, and social news from all over the country.

The work of "Shen Shi" originally focused on telegraphic news, aiming to compete with foreign telegraphic news agencies. However, it also paid great attention to lengthy correspondence from home and abroad, hoping to supplement the insufficiency of telegraphic news with systematic narration. All specially contracted correspondents have been deployed in almost all important cities, and correspondents in various remote provinces have been hired to send important news from the frontiers. Travel reporters have been repeatedly dispatched to inspect the northeastern and northwestern provinces and the Yangtze and Pearl River basins, collecting news related to the national economy and the people's livelihood. When the Fujian Incident occurred, personnel were sent to fly to Guangdong, Fujian, and the Zhejiang border to inspect the truth. When internal disputes often arose in Xinjiang, special personnel were contracted to enter Xinjiang from Baotou and Suiyuan to conduct on-the-spot investigations. Recently, personnel were sent to the bandit areas in Jiangxi Province to produce accurate accounts. The local news coverage in Shanghai focuses on political facilities, diplomatic transformations, the rise and fall of urban finance and rural economy, the movement of social consciousness and people's livelihood patterns, adhering to the principle of emphasizing quality over quantity, and rejecting rumors. In addition, photography and plate-making departments were added to create vivid descriptions of current affairs issues. In response to requests from various newspapers in the interior, a lightweight stereotype machine was specially created to allow various news photographs to be published in newspapers in areas where transportation is blocked, with extremely economical and swift procedures. Other efforts include assisting newspapers in various regions, managing advertising and sales, organizing investigations and publishing to seek newspaper contact. "Shen Shi" is happy to make efforts and implement any undertaking that is beneficial to our newspaper industry.

In February of this year, "Shen Shi" further sought organizational integrity, formally organized a limited liability company in accordance with the Company Law, collected sufficient funds, and established a board of directors. Mr. Du Yuesheng, Mr. Li Shuxiong, Mr. Yu Zuoting, Mr. Zhang Xiaoru, Mr. Xiao Tongzi, Mr. Zhang Zhuping, Mr. Dong XianGuang, Mr. Pan Gongbi, and Mr. Mi Xingru were elected as directors, and Mr. Zhang Yishu and Mr. Song Chunfang were elected as supervisors. The application for government registration was submitted and approved on May 26, and the Ministry of Industry issued license number 715. Branch offices were established in Beijing, Hankou, Tianjin, and Hong Kong in accordance with the original plan. At the same time, the internal structure of the head office was reorganized, the scope of business was expanded, equipment was further improved, and the organization was further strengthened, with the aim of providing better services and more progressive cooperation for newspapers in various regions.

2. Current Organization

Since "Shen Shi" has been legally established as a formal limited liability company, the current organization is entirely in accordance with the provisions of the Company Law. Nine directors are elected by the shareholders' meeting to form the board of directors, representing the company in the execution of important business and bearing the responsibility for supervision and control. Two supervisors are selected to perform supervisory duties. The board of directors appoints a general manager and a president of the head office, who execute the resolutions of the board of directors, handle the affairs of the news agency, and represent the news agency externally. Currently, there are seven departments. The duties of each department are summarized as follows: (1) Telegraphic News Department, divided into (A) Interviewing, responsible for contacting, liaising with, and managing telegraphic news interviewers in various regions; (B) Receiving Telegrams, responsible for registering Chinese and Western telegrams, long-distance telephone calls, and wireless radio broadcasts; (C) Translating Telegrams, responsible for translating Chinese and Western telegrams and proofreading telegrams; (D) Editing, editing Chinese and Western telegrams; (E) Sending Telegrams, responsible for sending Chinese and Western wired and wireless telegrams, long-distance telephone calls, and wireless radio broadcasts, and registering sent telegrams; (2) Postal News Department, divided into (A) Interviewing, responsible for contacting, liaising with, and managing local field reporters, travel reporters in various regions, specially contracted correspondents in various regions, and postal news interviewers in various regions; (B) Editing, editing local news and correspondence from other cities; (C) Writing and Printing, responsible for writing, proofreading, printing, and binding; (D) Delivery, responsible for delivering local news and sending manuscripts to other cities and abroad; (3) Photography Department, responsible for taking photos of current affairs, celebrities, and landscapes; (4) Advertising Department, divided into (A) Soliciting and introducing advertisements; (B) Designing and drafting advertisements; (C) Investigating and statistically analyzing advertisements; (5) Plate-Making Department, responsible for making lead plates, stereotype plates, paper plates, and lightweight stereotype machines; (6) Publishing Department, divided into (A) Editing, printing, and distributing regular or irregular publications; (B) Investigating and planning publishing matters; (7) Administrative Department, divided into (A) Accounting, responsible for economic receipts and expenditures; (B) General Affairs, responsible for purchasing and keeping items; (C) Documentation, responsible for official documents and correspondence; (D) Operations, responsible for contacting and promoting various operations; (E) Others, responsible for matters not belonging to other departments. There are also other emerging businesses that are being gradually organized in response to the needs of the times. They will not be described in detail.

3. Future Prospects

The commencement of "Shen Shi's" business was based on the convenience of the newspaper industry and its balanced development. The gradual development of its business to date has been due to the spirit of "not seeking private gain." This principle has been upheld without fail over the past decade and will continue to be upheld consistently in the future without any change. However, in view of the increasingly severe foreign aggression and the critical state of the country, foreign news businesses are taking advantage of their deep history and strong power to perform great spectacles in the international arena. Our colleagues in the newspaper industry bear a heavy responsibility in this difficult era, which goes without saying. The colleagues of "Shen Shi" are aware of the importance of their mission and will continue to serve the spirit of the newspaper industry in the future. In addition to further expanding existing business and striving to be the most faithful and effective news agency in the country, they will make further preparations for the unity of the nation and the revitalization of the country, and need to unite communication agencies and newspapers operated by Chinese people in order to compete with foreign communication agencies on the international stage. This is the greatest goal of "Shen Shi's" progress. The Associated Press of the United States and the United Press of Japan are good examples of successful integration in the newspaper industry. The colleagues of "Shen Shi" humbly wish to discuss this with wise people at home and abroad today, as they recall the past decade of struggle.

Free Talk

On the Family 211

— Chuan Ru

Speaking of "family," there was a joke about it long ago. When I was in Beiping, a Western professor at a certain university, explaining the Chinese character for "family," said it meant a house filled with pigs, and that was the Chinese family. Of course, the university students in the audience were outraged, thinking the Western professor was intentionally insulting them, and as a result, he was expelled. So some people said that Westerners don't understand Chinese etymology, so they misinterpreted the character for "family." In fact, according to the great etymological work, the "Shuowen Jiezi," the character for "family" is derived from the radical 宀 (roof), and the phonetic component 豭 (boar) is abbreviated. Zhou Bowen said: the pen where pigs live is called a family, hence it is composed of 宀 and 豕 (pig). Later generations borrowed it to mean the family household. The Western professor's explanation was not wrong. Aren't 豭 and 豕 the same meaning?

The ancient Chinese family was not only very different from the small, one-husband-one-wife family of today, but also very different from the old-style large families that included fathers, sons, wives, brothers, uncles, aunts, and sisters-in-law. At that time, the family was almost like a small country, as in the so-called "family with a thousand chariots" or "family with a hundred chariots." Even now, these most ancient forms of families are not completely gone. Look at someone who becomes rich, and the people who eat with him number in the hundreds or thousands. Many of them can be idle without doing anything, holding the title of family retainer, and can get odd jobs at any time. Thus, the family becomes large, and the country suffers!

The most advanced people now are becoming members of society, while we are still clinging tightly to being members of a family. As the saying goes, "One person has good fortune, and it extends to the whole house." I don't know what lives under this roof?

The "Great Learning" says: "Those who wish to govern their state must first regulate their families." Chapter 9 says: "If his family cannot be taught, how can he teach others?" From this, it can be seen the importance of the family in terms of morality. Originally, regulation and teaching are troublesome things enough. To regulate and teach, one must nourish them richly, so everyone harbors selfishness and only cares about expanding the scope of their own family wealth. There are also some people who click their tongues and envy them, saying: "So-and-so's family fortune is not small!" Once so-and-so's family fortune is not small, then "one family doesn't cry, but the whole road cries loudly!" Alas, I have seen too much of this!

There is a wonderful metaphor for this. It is said that the Chinese family is like a locomotive, with a string of fancy cars, passenger cars, and even baggage cars and freight cars behind it. Of course, the locomotive is the head of the family. The locomotive rushes back and forth, sweating and exhausted. Sometimes it is too hard, and it feels like it can't pull it anymore, so it stops for a moment and sighs a few strange noises (the whistle)! If it is unhappy, the locomotive suddenly goes off the rails, and everything behind it will die a violent death.

So what should we do? We should no longer be locomotives, but should fly airplanes through the sky. If we crash, only I die, and at most three or five people die with me. This means that we should no longer sacrifice for the family, and we should no longer strive to expand our own family wealth. We should be free members of society! Otherwise, those who are related to our family cannot avoid

being pigs under the roof!

The Heat in Nanjing (1) 212

— Shushan

Hot, hot, hot, this has almost become the universal cry of this summer.

Only because I am still enduring the heat in Nanjing, I don't know what the heat is like elsewhere. Just as people elsewhere certainly don't know exactly what the heat in Nanjing is like, I will, in between wiping away sweat, report the heat in Nanjing to the readers.

The weather in Nanjing, since the beginning of summer, has been the hottest in thirty years. Tracing back from the 24th of last month to today, in these 20 days, there was only one heavy rain on the evening of the 1st of this month, and the temperature quickly increased. Until the 5th, the indoor temperature reached 104 degrees Fahrenheit. Although it decreased slightly on the 10th, it still reached 98.5 degrees. However, on the 11th, it suddenly increased to 103 degrees. The intense heat has been even more severe these last two days. Yesterday, at noon, the indoor temperature rose to 102 degrees, and in the afternoon it continued to rise, reaching 108.5 degrees. Being in the room feels like being in a fiery pit, and it is difficult to endure even for a moment.

With such a drought and such heat, it is no wonder that the farmers are crying in distress. They have tried various methods to pray for rain, such as burning incense, worshiping Buddha, or parading with tied dragons. In fact, even though we live in the city, we also long for the early arrival of sweet rain to relieve the drought and heat, don't we? These past few days, just because the signs of disaster have already formed, rice has suddenly increased from one stone to more than two yuan, and vegetables have also doubled in price. We can't seal our mouths and not eat, or tighten our belts and not be hungry, so of course we are waiting for rain just like the farmers. Moreover, with this intense heat in the city, it feels like being steamed by the heat in a steamer, making it unbearable. It is necessary to have a heavy rain to dissipate it.

After all, this rare disaster is enough to move the compassionate heart of the living Buddha. This is the Panchen Lama, who returned after presiding over the Kalachakra Dharma Assembly for disaster relief and saving the country at West Lake. He couldn't bear to see the suffering of all living beings, so he wanted to move the will of heaven with his Buddhist teachings. Therefore, he set up altars everywhere to recite scriptures and pray for rain. It's just that the will of heaven was stubborn and refused to comply. Moreover, he was sweating and panting under the fiery canopy of the fire god, and had no way to resist the heat. Finally, he left Nanjing today, probably to escape the heat and go to Beiping. Although it is said that he will continue to pray for rain for us after he arrives in Beiping.

Literature and Self 213

— Dongsheng

The American literary critic Henry Neumsch once said, "Literature is the tune of the individual's soul, literature is the symbol of the individual's will." This statement is of course a bit of an overstatement, but we can admit that, in literary works, the spirit of the self deeply dominates. A literary work is nothing more than a "recording of the subjective impression of objective things," a "manifestation of the spirit of the self in the consciousness of the times." When the author's mind and the things in the environment cause a reflection, during the time of conceiving consciousness, the spirit of the self unconsciously assumes a strong force. Reading the author's work is no different from being guided by the author's thoughts, being influenced by the author's emotions. For example, reading Lermontov's poems, there are

bold rhymes, and in the strength of the words, you can hear the sound of swords. Jutcheff's poems have a strange and mysterious meaning, just like the ancient prophets speaking a

kind of terrifying and dangerous language in the middle of the night. Nekrasov's poems are crude and profound

tones, the intense emotions of damaged humanity, the lament of a disturbed conscience. Byron Shelley's poems are full of romantic and gorgeous qualities, while Uut U's new poems have a natural and profound flavor. When we read their poems, it is as if we see their people. The arrangement of words implies the leaping of their hearts, because in their works, their personalities are expressed, their spirits are revealed. Every great writer has his own special style, and we can also say that only those works that faithfully and without any hypocrisy express the secrets of one's own soul are successful and great products of the spirit.

Musset said, "Each person has his own wine glass. Although I drink from a small glass, this glass is mine!" Friends! Remember this sentence! Use your thoughts to write what you want to write. Don't look down on yourself too much. Don't you remember what Goethe said in a poem called "Self-Awareness"?

No matter who you are 丨丨 this is without distinction,

You 丨丨 are always a person, please do not demean yourself,

Look at yourself 丨丨 you yourself must say, that's right!

Becoming yourself is the most important condition for obtaining spiritual rewards. Becoming yourself is satisfying yourself. Becoming yourself is also denying yourself. Don't you remember Ibsen's words?

Kill the self within your heart.

And listen to becoming yourself 丨丨 that is 丨丨

Express yourself forever,

That master is willing to use what you express.

Friends! To put it concretely, becoming yourself is to develop the power accumulated in your heart and those abilities that have been feared, suppressed, and exploited by habits and traditions regarding the independence of the soul. That power and ability are the raw materials for your work, which can allow you to achieve a little, albeit weak, but glorious success.

What is written in violation of the soul and conscience is insignificant and base. You must always express yourself with yourself! Reject all forms of power, remove all arrogant attitudes, believe in yourself, regardless of gains and losses. If you think something can be revealed, you might as well reveal it. Remember Goethe's words as sung in "Der Sänger":

I sing clearly here,

Like a little bird singing on a branch,

The song bursts forth from my own throat,

This is my supreme reward.

In conclusion, I respectfully offer this little poem to the writers of today.

"Although the sound is small, it must come from your own throat," as Musset said:

"Each person has his own wine glass. Although I use a small wine glass, this glass is mine."

July 14th 214

— Zhili

This year's French National Day celebration in Shanghai was particularly lively, as reported in the Shen Bao:

"This year's lanterns and decorations are even more splendid than in previous years. The French Consulate, the Municipal Council, various police stations, fire brigades, health departments, the French barracks, and the Gujiazhai Garden are all covered in lanterns and decorations. The area around Rue du Consulat is especially dazzling and colorful. The huge lantern towers and arches in the ancient Chinese style at the three locations of Avenue Joffre, Route Cardinal Mercier, and the Eight Immortals Bridge are attracting tourists to stop and watch."

But under such splendid circumstances, those who rush to join in the fun are mostly Chinese. As Mr. Taisheng recorded in "New Shanghai":

"Night, pushing open the brilliantly lit, French National Day carnival.

Everywhere flew the red, blue, and white French flags. On the streets, strings of yellow-faced people, the ruled in this secondary colony.

On Rue Lafayette, a row of children, women, women in vests with cross-straps, young people in fashionable white pants, with green French park tickets and yellow French park

passes in their palms.

Hearts are so hot, blowing the cool July night wind. At the entrance of the French Park, the fire trees are painted with red and green lights

. On both sides, people rushed straight to the entrance from the intersection.

It's the French carnival! The yellow-faced people all pushed aside the defense line of the Qinglian-colored armed police as if they didn't care about their lives, rushed past the guard of the Annamese yellow-armed people, rushed! Rushed inside! These crazy yellow-faced people, pushing the cross-straps on the fashionable vests, pushing the fur coats of the old ladies, rushed through the defense line at the entrance from the crowded lane of yellow-faced people.

Look: the lights are brilliant, the French carnival in this city that never sleeps!

Crazy yellow-faced people! This is the French carnival

! These pitiful people who are ruled, have actually forgotten that this is the French National Day garden!"

The yellow-faced people are indeed people who love to join in the fun. Their joining in the fun is just joining in the fun, no matter what the fun is about. Who cares if it's the French National Day? In short, it's much more lively than the Chinese Republic's National Day, and that's good enough. Conversely, if it weren't for so many yellow-faced people rushing to join in the fun, then the "huge lantern towers and arches in the ancient Chinese style" would be set up in vain. And this, from the rulers' point of view, is sharing the joy with the people (the rulers), giving grace, and at the same time asking for gratitude and support. Therefore, under the "Great Self-Ringing Bell" on Rue du Consulat, there are two slogans: Vive la France! (Long live France!) and Vive la garde municipale de Shanghai! (Long live the municipal guard of Shanghai!) However, in the situation of "fire trees and silver flowers, the city opens and never sleeps," who is "indulging in intoxication and losing their minds"? It's not just the yellow-faced people. Even the citizens of French democracy, when they see the huge lantern towers and arches in the ancient Chinese style, would they ever think about why this arch was erected and remember the situation in Paris on July 14th, one hundred and forty-five years ago?

The situation in Paris on July 14th, one hundred and forty-five years ago, was roughly as follows:

"The people of Paris were already prepared. On the evening of the 13th, teams of armed people approached the Bastille fortress and exchanged gunfire with the guards. On the morning of the 14th, they gathered in large numbers on the road leading to the Bastille. They also had cannons, which they had seized from the Invalides; they also had guns and gunpowder, which they had searched for in cellars and churches; some were holding spears, halberds, hammers, and axes, and some even only had simple wooden sticks. The commander of the fortress looked down from the top of the wall and saw that the entire streets and alleys of the Saint-Antoine district were a black mass, and the heads of the rioters were approaching like waves. The roar was like a tidal wave, saying: "We want the Bastille fortress! Lower the drawbridge!" The commander was almost dizzy with fright at this situation.

"The first outer drawbridge of the Bastille was soon broken. The crowd poured into the commander's office. The guards of the Bastille opened fire to resist, and the two sides fired for more than three hours. Many people in the crowd were killed or wounded, but they were not afraid at all and continued to besiege in various ways. At the same time, the people of the entire city of Paris rose up, carrying cannons,

to provide support.

Finally, the guards surrendered. The commander handed over the key to the door of the inner drawbridge. The crowd occupied the fortress and released the prisoners buried in the prison. At this time, the emotions were very agitated. When the crowd saw the appearance of the prisoners, they shed tears. When the prisoners saw the sunlight and heard the cheers of the crowd welcoming their release from prison, they even fainted." (See Xu Maoyong: History of the French Revolution, New Life Popular Library edition.)

Thinking about it, this situation was more lively than July 14th in Shanghai in 1934. But what is the difference between these two kinds of liveliness? July 14th in Paris one hundred and forty-five years ago, French rioters destroyed the Bastille fortress, which represented French feudal politics. On the same day one hundred and forty-five years later, French rulers in Shanghai were sharing joy with the yellow-faced people, and among them were also the ruled French citizens.

The July 14th celebration created by the Parisian sans-culottes was seized by the French bourgeoisie, ordering "universal celebration" and supporting the French Republic forever. Thus, even the yellow-faced people were joining in the fun under the lanterns.

However, the only kind of fun that the yellow-faced people of Shanghai seem to be good at joining in is this kind.

A Wall (6) 215

— Original by Roberto Bracco, translated by Xi Dichen

He draped his huge coat around him, hobbled away with his bad leg, muttering between gasps, "Go, go beg for food, go beg for food!"

The young man stood at the table, motionless, but calm and composed, softly saying, "From today on, endure hunger!" But the slanderous article was never written. Why, for what reason, did he not write it? He couldn't say. He looked around. The blinds were still closed. It was still night in his room. From the street, from the neighboring houses, in the midst of the confused sounds of awakening, the new life of the day floated

softly, softly. The sewing machine stopped. The old, solid wall was once again impenetrable. The wall hadn't let the light of dawn

filter through. It hadn't let the obscene words that a drunk, using a jailer's key, said to the woman who had been awake all night permeate through. When he came in, he had said to her, "If you don't give me something to eat by noon, I'll wring your neck like a chicken!"

Now this drunken fellow was already asleep, sleeping soundly. The woman, with a bundle of machine-sewn shirts under her arm, was preparing to go out, pleased that she had a way to satisfy his wishes. Before leaving the room, she thought of her neighbor. Her poor happiness—even her life—was owed to his compassionate tolerance.

He gently knocked on the wall. The young man trembled, as he was sitting like an idiot, staring blankly at the blank white paper. "Beg for food? But the sewing machine saved me from defiling—from slandering—a good person—are you asking me to smile? Are you asking me to smi..."

He could hear the woman in the next room calling him, so he gently knocked on the wall in reply. Then both of them simultaneously pressed their lips to the wall, and simultaneously said:

"Thank you!"

Neither side heard this joyful word, because both mouths touched the separating wall at the same time. When each left

the wall, they both murmured to themselves:

"It wasn't her!"

"It wasn't her!"
